Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the mouse disease according to what we have discussed in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help, then there are three kinds of cauteries that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which one way is that you make three, or four, cauteries along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery we spoke of before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient often be on their back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart that is near the mouse, or the patient's ribs come towards the left, and let the elevation where you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the breadth of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	Afterwards, put the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you wish, cauterize with the entire cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure, when it has cast off corruption for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does no good, then you must apply four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one on the breast.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cauteries be close to the depth of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to allow for the discharge of pus for a long time, and do not abandon the patient's treatment after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would be hastened, and both intentions would be joined together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly should be the shape we have previously shown.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And the one for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what was described earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in someone with dropsy, and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and annular bones.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, lest the yellow water be forced out, and let the cauteries be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Then make two cauteries on each leg, at the tip of the calf.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries open for a long time without dressing, so that the water comes out;
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the inflammation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When the loosening of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the virtues of retention and digestion that are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the sick person suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make a large cautery on the stomach, according to what has been spoken about previously, or the circular cautery of the stomach;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and four small cauteries around the abdomen, one small cauterizing cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach next to the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and are of large, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in the divisions, and it does no good, then make cauteries:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Three on the spine of the back, the one that is entirely outside the navel, little by little in a triangular shape, and one cautery below the abdomen, two inches.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you think his stomach is chilled, and the food does not cook, and you see the face swelling, then put one large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen, a cautery on all the ribs.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	And leave the cautery open a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, leave the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness that is called "thelul".
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut the althelul, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then place it, all ablaze, onto the cut althelul.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and hold it there with your hand until the cautery reaches the source of the vein, where the blood flows.
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	Do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said.
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	After which, apply healing ointments until they are healed.
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	And if you cauterize with a large cautery over the wound, it will provide greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, as we will describe in its place, a sickness arises that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula appears on someone, and is old and discharges rottenness and corrupt moisture, you should apply a very thin covering over it, and take note how deep the covering reaches.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	Afterward, heat the cautery, which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula to the same depth as the covering had entered.  Continue the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the amount needed.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And be careful not to burn the nearby nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula extends to the bladder or the intestine, be careful around those areas and only apply the burn to the fleshy parts, and make sure that it doesn't go too deep.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	Afterward, treat the area until it is healed. If the area is sealed and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is infected and the bone at the bottom is corrupted.
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And thus, as one of those that we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and does not take the form of a woman, then you must cauterize the kidneys on either side with the clavicle cautery that we have previously described.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will provide greater help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is weak and cold and moist, so that the patient retains urine, then apply a cautery to the outside of the bladder, where the hair of the knife begins, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the nail of a thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and apply one cautery to the back outside, or two if necessary.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cauteries be shaped according to the form previously mentioned.
de la marris	Of the spleen.
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the spleen is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain.
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	Then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the abdomen, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauteries be small, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous humours descend into the socket of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	And when the place of the separation is found empty, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one cautery shaped like a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and let the cauteries be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After that, apply cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cautery is in two ways:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is in many ways, of which one is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make it deep and wide, and have a space of a finger's width between each cautery, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes cautery is done in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four of them according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the thick parts of the center are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain is in the hip, and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it goes down to the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle, four inches, a little to the left side;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cauteries be cut-like, and let the thick parts of the center be burned;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels the pain extend down to an inch or near the heel, cauterize there where he feels the pain, three or four points, with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, then make more.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if you know the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, make a cut-like or circular cautery, and be very careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have applied cautery to the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot also, and the entire foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the bowels, from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men said, regarding the cautery of the hip, this is the manner: make a tool like this, and let it be as thick as a fingertip, or a little less, and have divisions, and let it be from one division to the other, the space of a finger's width.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the divisions be facing in two directions, and be like notches, and there be a handle of iron well made;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And it should be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then it is placed on the sore hip, and turned to the healthy side;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and cauterize it once, the cautery heals, and leave it for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its effect, and we see few who use it;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless this is a good cautery, which can endure it, and the place where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make a tool with crossbars, in which the edge of the door descends, and it should be of bronze or iron with one long side, and have two grooves, and have between each the thickness of a finger;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and they should be open at the front and above, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Then place the hot box on the patient's side lying on their healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the patient's hip;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	then pour between the two circles of hot water that has been heated over the fire a little bit, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and the burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For it finds there a burning sensation as if from fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the burning is gone, remove your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with soft water, and leave it like this for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the burn is removed;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and leave it three days to allow the corruption to come out;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and that would be the final help after the treatment of ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain extends to the thigh or to the leg, make one instrument to apply water according to what you did for the hip similarly;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of hot water, and I have written it in the treatment of the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small hole to allow the point of a razor to enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and place over that pot another pot well sealed, and put on alkali and lime and sweet water on top, until there is a thumb's breadth of it above the powders once you have held it firmly in your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it thus until the water descends and drips into the sealed pot, then take all that water, and pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical works and in cauterizations of other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does the work of fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip, such as turpentine and honey of acacia and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen recounts a cure with which a man was cured of hip and sciatic pain, and greatly praises it, saying that no other cure was made, and that he was healed in a single time when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And says in this way that you take fresh and dry green litharge, and grind it finely with a bit of grease, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bind it on.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it on for three hours, and by the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly moistened, and put him into bed, and the pain will depart entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such remedies unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps a lot;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and the cauteries must be made in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe and the other, which is called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After that, take dry goat's dung, and burn it in fire until it is embers, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished;
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do it again in this way, and do not cease to do so until you think by your senses that it has reached the hip, and that the pain has stopped;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this method of cautery is called "cautery of goats".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or striking or from too great an evacuation, or from the spreading of cold matter, none of these appearances is worth cauteries, except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary, after the patient has been rid of foul pills or other similar things, that three lines of incisions be made on his back, where the pain is, and on each line five cauteries or more, according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and the cauteries should be done according to the cautery called "pricks";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you wish, make 3 or 4 cauteries at the middle nail-cautery, according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this illness comes to young children, and the sign of its beginning is that they have a tight chest when they rise, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find it in the last spine of the back, and in those which appear on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery grasps each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a cautery that pricks two or three lines, and let the pricks be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer cautery in a swelling that is in a nerve's pathway.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pains in the joints are from moisture spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the physicians properly call "podagra", and when it is from a cold cause and cures from medicines cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the sole of the foot, then make a cautery all over the cautery that is called "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains extend to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make three or four cauteries on each knee, on each part, all in the olive-shaped cautery form;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand too long, so that only the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have described in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then make pricks around the fossa, two lines;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains any pain in the fingers, then make pricks on each joint and on the skin of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains reach the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge the phlegm, he will be healthy with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the tearing of the skin
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the swelling descends to the testicles and it is recent, then when you wish to treat it, he should not eat anything that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he use things that loosen the belly, so that the stool descends from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the swelling subsides, and bring the swelling to your fingers, and make a sign underneath the rupture, over the bone of the groin, and make a whole sign that is like half a circle above the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery with this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and emits sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then return the bowels to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and let the assistant hold his hand over them so they do not return back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and properly open the patient's thighs, and place a cushion beneath him and an attendant upon the thighs, and another upon the chest who holds his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then place the cautery upon the mark with your whole hand, hold it straight, and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, begin again another time until you reach the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and carefully guard that the bowel does not burst when you do the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that by this the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their size, and of large people also large according to their size;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days treat the cautery site with butter until the burn is removed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after which apply other ointments until it is healed, and the patient should lie on their back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his nourishment be light for a long time, so that his belly does not swell when he gets up to go to the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after 40 days, when he wishes to get up, provide him with a well-made bandage, and keep it on for 40 more days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and have good rest, let him do little work and guard against excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he follows this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are no longer growing, apply a cautery cauterization according to its quantity, and let a third of the core be burned;
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a cautery in three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and put your hand in the middle, covering the entire cautery with your hand.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not helpful, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery that is called "points," and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb, and its smallness, weakness, virtue, location of twisting, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if not, repeat another cautery on that one, for such is the custom that it must change to the limb that is next to it, therefore you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of the art of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mixtures are sometimes aided by cautery, greatly aiding those illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see it cauterized, watch if the illness is in its beginning stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or stay, and you doubt that the corruption may seize the whole patient, then give five cauteries to the head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	One in the middle of the head, and the other toward the forehead at the end of the hair;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and leave your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors may escape;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize the mice according to what is in front of it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mildew is scattered everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and if it loses its clarity, then you must cauterize it with the cauteries we have described, one cautery on the nose, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the rump and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the buttocks, that you do not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and sometimes one cauterizes on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more aid you give him, and the more benefit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the sick person does not feel any pain at the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the types of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, apply the place with flour of figs with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauteries be a little into the depth of the core;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And sometimes cauterization is done to the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and however, no one should intervene if they are not knowledgeable of the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is advanced, and the tools of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deeply, according to the thickness of the core, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a colon and blood of an almond, of each a part;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be mixed together, and be bound with a cloth, and be left to air in the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen several times;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And a more correct thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said in the matter of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a sickness called "adubelati", and it delays in healing, either due to the superfluity it causes or because of the patient's age when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and they have little blood, or because of the time;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you wish to hasten its healing:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery with which this form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of that ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it from outside in such a manner that the course of the decay is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment by fire iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of ailment exists, called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a consumption of a limb, for it eats away at the limbs like fire eats dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this ailment in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the ailment is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After cauterizing all around until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply to the cauterized areas a poultice with oil until the heat from the fire is gone, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if not, then recommence the cautery on whatever parts remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this sore has sometimes been treated with sharp medicine instead of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already stated the treatment of sharp medicine in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often it happens that on the feet, due to external causes, a disease called "clos" arises, according to our understanding, and is a large, enclosed thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Cautery of fire is that you heat a cautery iron, just as a piece of iron, and it should be made of good iron to the size that it can wrap around the nail on all sides, and that it have fine edges;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After that, put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it thus for three days until it begins to shed pus;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make him a poultice of wild mallows crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with an ointment containing healing herbs until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by outward fires, and it often happens in hands and feet, then you must apply a cautery of hot water there;
et est en teil maniere:	and is in such a manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a copper or iron rod, or a blade of steel, and place it over the nail and the ingrowing nail, that is to say for corns;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and place the rod so that it covers it all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and the hot water can find a deep path down to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient endure a little the burning of the hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it like this, and it will detach itself completely from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another until you have removed all those that are on the body, then cure them with ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from a quartan fever or other, you must make four cauteries, or four, on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine;
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	This will stop the trembling, and the health of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	of foul-smelling pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes, foul-smelling pustules appear on the body, which come from corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	If they appear, then one should make a cautery on each head of the pustule.
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is heated in the fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes, they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluities from which they came are broken, and they are healed.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times great flows of blood occur from the artery that is cut in the wound that comes from the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	And it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nevertheless, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it firmly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more drops issue.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then place the olive-shaped cauteries, several small and large ones, into the fire until they are all red-hot.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps out forcefully when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do this, one after the other, until the blood is stopped.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when blood gushes from the artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong tying of thread, or by medicines applied that have the power to stop blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and be bound and held tight.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a stoppage by tightly binding with cloths or putting burning things on, or other similar things, will not be of much profit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to someone and they have no styptic or medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein, as we have said, and extend it well until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and not move the finger, but wet it often with cold water that is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and do inquiries beforehand about what cauteries and medicines are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	In the first chapter, we have told you all the diseases in which fire cautery, or burning medicines, are necessary, and the reasons and causes, and the instruments and forms of cauteries;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have arranged that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed through this chapter in the same way so that one can more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, my dear son, you must understand that this chapter has more peril and fear than the first on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to be cured.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	so come those who become so angry with their illness that they die easily due to the frenzy they find in their sickness, and from the severity of its malice;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there are some who give you their insight, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	wait, I am cured";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the sickness is despicable.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater consideration on your honor than on your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely regarding those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can obtain praise.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients, so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and lasting remembrance.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	My dearest son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and may you be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in divisions, in accordance with what precedes, or the chapter on cauteries, which I have described from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this illness often comes to children during childbirth, and when the attendant presses too hard on the child's head;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and in all those I have seen, death was quick.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And therefore, it seems to me that it is better to abandon this type of treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and whose head grew bigger each day until it could no longer support it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture gathered beneath the bone on the surface, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the treatment is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you should make a wide incision in the head;
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should be as long as two fingers, until the moisture drains.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see here the form of the spatula.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs are that you see the sutures of the head open on each side, and the pus bursts out when you press it with your hand inside, and this has not been resolved:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is necessary to split the head into three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture outward.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Afterwards, bind the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil on them, and leave it like this until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then unbind it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another manner of incision is that you look at the extent of the abscess, and the collection of the water;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind;
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut where the abscess is open, and the filling of water, and cut it according to what you are able to;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the outflow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of phlegm
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or chest, and the illness is longstanding, and the cure of medicine is of no benefit, then the final cure is cauterization, with which one would cauterize the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you wish to cauterize them, that the patient tilt their head back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterward, he rubs the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient tightens their neck with the whole cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look where the vein flows, and the locations of both are near the ears, and the places are made ready;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	then mark the spots, then cut both with a sharp knife from two sides, until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be at the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you want, place the knife under the artery and cut above it, cutting as you should across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts continuously outward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery is not apparent to the touch, then you must measure the space of three fingers, then mark and cut down to the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and what is necessary to evacuate of blood is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate, and the fullness of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if there remains on the bone any sign of suppuration, cut it so that no hot abscesses arise, then bind and bandage the wound, and apply an ointment cure until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and chronic madness and similar things, and he is treated with various medical cures and none of it benefits him, then we will draw blood from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of drawing from them is that the patient pull back the hair of their temples and look for the artery that is visible in the temple, for it shows itself by its beating, and is hardly visible, except in some very cold men;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is visible, the patient tightens their neck with some cloths, then rubs the area with a rough cloth, and warms the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the lancet, of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues underneath on each side;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is slender, you turn it with the point of the hook, then cut it in that part according to the amount of the two ends.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not completely stop.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw blood from VI to III;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that no decay comes before the wound heals, and blood does not flow out;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then cut the excess that is between the two ligatures at that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the knife cautery to the bone until the ends are cut;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is a difficult task, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauterization is a help to finish the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for this reason it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill the place with old cotton and place on well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when one loosens them, they should be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until they are healed;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if without cutting the artery while you work on it, you hurry to cut it with cautery, or you fill the place with vitriol and hold it with your hand so that the blood is stopped;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this present, place your finger on the place until the blood is congealed, and wash the place with cold water until the blood stops, and it is constrained as it should be;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And the method that is gentler and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from two sides, but the cutting edges should be wide to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be one finger's breadth of space between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two places, you place the burning iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they should be separated between the two ends, because it is not completely soldered by this cautery.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears from the eyes are flowing down the veins on the head's surface, and no medicinal treatment helps, and you see the patient's face turn red, and feel a trembling sensation on the forehead;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if the skin is thin and moist, so that the hairs of the eyelashes have fallen out, and the eyelids are inflamed and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contusive treatment," and it is that you make the patient's hair on the forehead recede, and then make three equal cuts on the forehead along the length of the forehead;
