et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the cuts should be just below the middle of the forehead down to the nose, and the other two are along either side of the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries along either side of the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the junction of the two jaws, and each wound should be the width of three fingers across the joint;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have a piece of sponge and plenty of cloths ready to wipe the blood, then apply the pointed spatula from two directions, like this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision by the temple down to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the flesh between the two cuts to all the surface that is on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then put in the first cut the instrument called "cultellaire", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not sharp, and this is the shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the cutting side of the knife towards the flesh, close to the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and put it in until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where it emerges from the heart, and then do the same in the middle cut up to the other end;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then remove blood equally, and press the place to collect the taken blood;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then place a tent of old cotton in each cut, and put over it cloths soaked in wine, oil and vinegar, and guard against the formation of hot abscesses;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, untie the bandage, and apply a large quantity of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used for wound healing, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the cold in the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When some are afflicted with an acute cold, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and vision weakening, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and there is sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know by these symptoms that the matter and this cold come from various veins, and the best treatment for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you tell the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another a wide one in the middle of the forehead.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the incision on the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the incision and place old cotton and linen strips there;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then tie over them cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with things that dry out and cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In such a way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stuffing of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or a beast, or a stone from a mine, or a similar thing like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as flax, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or something flowing, such as water and blood and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or another kind of thing falls into the ear that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then drop a little violet oil or oil of sesame, then administer extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make him sneeze with a condiment, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and extend the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often it comes out with this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out, administer extraction with subtle pincers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it leaps out with the pincers, that is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If not, administer extraction with a subtle, small double-edged hook;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump out with that, make a copper chain and put the head of the chain into the hole of the ear firmly, and seal what is around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out like we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in such a manner, take glue with which birds are caught, and place any instrument fitting for this on top, and put a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not jump out with all these things that we have said, hurry to pierce the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come to it;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of piercing is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fat or dependent area;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be like a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, administer a thin, subtle spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is made easier.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should use initial sneezing remedies, and the ear should be filled with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it dries up because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, take several stones according to the length of your finger, small and light, and warm them slightly in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and let the patient place one or several in the opening of their ear, and jump on it from the other side of their feet, and press another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to do this with stone on stone until the water comes out completely, and thus it will dry up completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end apply to fire until the most pliable part of the reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do the same with other reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said of the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In extracting a creature, if it is small, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms lodged in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment is of no use, you must look at the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if any worms appear, extract them with delicate tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the instrument of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow underneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the patient's suffering, then suck firmly on the entire instrument;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms exit.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to exit, stuff around the instrument with cotton, as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations which the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this entire instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And it is of silver or copper, narrow underneath with small holes, and wider above for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press the distillation into an instrument of well-made copper for this, and if you wish take a scraper and wrap around the tip with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the channel, and the channel be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then place the scraper inside the entire cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the end of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient smells it inside, and let the distillation be a little heated by fire before distilling it into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and watch that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffiness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without any holes in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through the stuffiness of a wound, or flesh growing inside the ear, and this stuffiness sometimes goes deep into the ear, so one cannot see it;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the pus flows out of the hole, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which goes deep, so that one cannot see it, is of grievous healing in many conditions, and in that which one sees, you must put the patient's ear in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the apparent blockage, then work on all this matter of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, perfectly smooth, so that it does not injure the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the blockage is of flesh born in or around the ear, then hold it with delicate forceps, and cut it lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the blockage is deep within the ear, then take a delicate, thin scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it within the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the blockage of which the patient complains of difficulty hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent within the ear, according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder it with crushed vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a discharge of blood comes, then dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the discharge of blood which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the ulcers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the ulcer that arises in ulcers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, then you must stretch them with forceps and pincers, and cut it with a spatula from its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put powdered vitriol on the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a thin lenticular cautery iron, and after the incision, cauterize again.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repeat, since something remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come in the eyes' papers things that seem like hail in its shape and hardness, and for this, this disease is called "grandine," and is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below;
li ovraiges est telz:	the work is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	beware if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then cut it [the grandine] along the length, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with pincers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing the paper a bit, do not worry the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, assemble it with a suture and treat it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment will quickly restore it and create flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the granulation is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and extend the granulation with pincers, and cut it and press it on either side;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved away by the incision, that does no harm;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the granulation is cut, raise the eye of salted water, and treat the place with what generates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is generated in webs of the eyelids, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and therefore they often lie on their faces, and sleep on their backs, and their eyelids beneath their eyebrows are moist, that the swelling and appearance have covered with the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the method of treatment is that the patient places their head on your chest;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over it;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on either side, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut a slit in the middle of the moisture, using a sharp spatula, a slit not wider than the incision made during bloodletting;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many places exinach comes from the slit, in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then, pull it out with a whole piece of cloth held between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and be careful not to force into the slit, so you don't reach the whole spatula to the eye, and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, then slightly enlarge the slit a little until it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then pull it out as we have said, then soak cloths in oil and water, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And some people grind seeds and apply them to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess forms at the site, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of the papillary region.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When additional hairs grow on the eyelids, other than those natural to them, and they age, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, like habitual tearing and softening of the eyelids and conjunctiva, until this is a cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the treatment is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine, according to what is before or in the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching, or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You should place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then you put a needle with thread above it;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be next to the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and draw the thread above the entire eyelid, and turn it with a razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part under the eyelid, under the hairs attached, along the entire septum, from the large tear duct down to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then paint a figure of a bandage on the eyelid, like the leaf of myrtle, and however it should be the size you want to elevate the eyelid, which is divided in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is such a need that a large quantity of the eyelid is cut according to the softening of the eyelid;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then cut along the entire septum on the two lines you have drawn, and begin from the large tear duct down to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, the thickness of a root, then insert the hook into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape it all off;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle and fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and let the excess thread dry on the two eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you wish to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then take no further care, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constricting things, for the paper peels off at the healing of the wound and its coming together, but the stitches are milder (as the ancients said), and this is a safe procedure;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you draw the paper in a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three separate points according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above in small equal forces, according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the strength to hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread and put it in the middle of the shape;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the leather on which you have drawn, as we have described, then assemble the two edges of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is healthy;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if so, you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of the canes is thus according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the paper and the slit within according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two thin strips as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two heads from two sides where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly over what protrudes of the paper of the eye, and hold the two canes of the two parts firmly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is held will die and dry and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, then cut it with some force, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is closed, and the paper will be removed, and the hair will no longer prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and thread a fine and soft silk thread into it;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the ends and knot them subtly, and the length of the threads should be a palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then neatly arrange another fine silk thread in the chase, and knot the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then place the patient's head on your lap;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be beside the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a delicate and minute work, then insert the needle throughout the chase into the hair root immediately, and pierce the paper quickly until you draw it over the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the chase, and put that hair into the chase, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then remove your hand so that the hairs come out of the entire chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the chase underneath along all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you will pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the flesh grows;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is small, then attach one long hair from the natural hairs, and let it grow with that one until it is lengthened and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness, called "aleacrati," or corruption, comes to the eye, there are two types of it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through the wounding of a cut, or a surgical incision, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the method of treatment is to split that scab, and separate its edges, and put linen strips inside, and bandage it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and you should not use things that dry and constrict in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the illness will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but use softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and water or cooked linseed and melted diachylon ointment in any oil, and wrap a bandage in it, and treat it with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your treatment is that you guard against it not healing according to its former shape;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these treatments that we have mentioned are only remedies to prevent this illness from returning in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds, cuts, cautery, and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the method of treatment is to take a needle, with double thread, and pierce the flesh, starting from the inner corner of the left eye and going all the way to the right, so that the thread comes out at two points in the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then stretch the flesh over the needle, and cut it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the paper's figure returns according to what is necessary, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take a scraper and place it in the incision, turn the paper, and make two incisions on the inside edge of the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the tips of the two incisions be at the two corners of the incision you have made, and make angles such that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "a Greek I";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the amount its edges are sharper under what covered the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a wool thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with the medicines that soften, and with poultices, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the ailment comes from an incision, or a suture, or cautery, you must make a full incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two edges of a poultice, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled masters devise remedies with all their power so that they can return the form to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what work and instruments are required in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	so suddenly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this joining happens to human hands in such a way that the paper on top is joined to the white of the eye, and cannot move or do its natural work, then you must put the point of a razor beneath the paper and lift it upwards;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and extend it with pincers, until you cut that which is airy in the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer the spatula to be too sharp and injure the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, with which you scrape that assembly, should be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and the entire assembly is healed, and sometimes they use sharp salty water, and lift it with sweet water, and with a collander;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and place moistened wool over the eye, abundant with egg;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use a collander and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembles a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, that when one touches it with iron and tries to pierce it, one cannot.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both likenesses begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient place their head in your lap, then open their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper with your hand, then grip the nail with small tweezers and extend it upward;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle and put a hair of horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and place it in the middle of the nail, and pierce it all the way through the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upward, and scrape with all the hair the side of the nail which is next to the pupil and the silk to the hair to the tip, then cut the remaining at the root of the tear duct with all the subtle spatulas and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct, so that with the incision the flow of tears does not come customarily;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail is extended with the forceps alone, and with thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one scrapes it with all the soft spatulas of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision put a little of bruised sil and lead-based concoction into the eye, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nerve-related, and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the lancet cannot enter, this type of nail is often cured with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye, and take a light, sharp spatula according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And carefully slice the nail, and if you see that it is thinning and the blood is close, then distil from your mouth into the eye a concoction of lead-based medicine, red medicine, and bruised sil, and bandage the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then resume the same procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary to you in the eye, like a boil, then leave it and treat the boil first until it is healed, then resume the procedure as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the eyelid tissue harms the eye with great damage, then suspend it with the forceps, and cut off a part, and not all of it, so that tears do not come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill red medicine made from lead into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men's eyes, flesh sometimes grows red, and covers the pupil and tightens over the eyelids, and resembles a rose-shaped, hard lump;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the procedure is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then opens their eyes, and you pick up all that flesh with appropriate forceps, and hold it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting with a scalpel until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the procedure;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And let the incision be done with the spatula as we described in the incision of the nail and with small forces to remove the scab, as the shape will demonstrate following this chapter;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, apply oil of crocus or distilled red ochre and similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and put a bandage of egg white over the eye to ensure against a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	And if anything remains, and the blood flows and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do for any flesh that has adhered to the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However, you must mitigate the treatment of each eye weak in its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Those are red veins that are covered over the eye, and they hinder the eye's work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, it is necessary first to look if the eye, in which the blood is, is strong, and there is no other illness except the blood;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then coil it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put their head in your bosom, then suspend those veins with a whole needle according to his wisdom, and let the needles be thin and double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two needles by degrees in one body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then coil those veins forcefully, and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins move strongly from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful not to pierce the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut anything but those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, distill green and red gall into the eye to corrupt what remains of the gravel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all of it at that time, make a plaster on the eye of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is calmed and an abscess is certainly hot, then recommence according to this manner that is before until it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with cautery and with burning sharp medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not yet healed, then you must open the abscess where it should fester and extract all the moisture in it until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then scrape it with all the instruments whose form is shown here;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and is called "rough head," and it should be made of iron and pointed at one end, and be pointed like a file, as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the area of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the area is healed, and flesh grows, and the body of the wound is healed, and it remains like this for forty days, and it does not regenerate and is not inflamed, and no bad accident happens, know that it is healthy;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, there is no other remedy than to lead the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, you take a drill according to this form, and let the iron head have three angles, and the shaft be narrowed to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because air escapes if he holds his hand over his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the area with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is then a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye's discharge
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance to the nose, nor a lessening, then you should bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then cleanse it, then apply cupping glasses or a haeterel without striking to draw out the fluid, then put over the eye a compress made of asafoetida, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolla, and then hold the eye shut and apply the plaster over it, bound with bandages and strips;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the strips is that you should take strips soft enough, and double each into four, and then place one over the other according to the quantity the eye needs;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then hold it shut with a hard bandage tightly, and repeat the cupping to draw out the fluid without striking;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye held shut day and night, and if the compress softens, you must hold it shut tightly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the compress after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then repeat the plaster, bandages, the compress, and cupping until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the tearing of the cloth or skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come in the skin/cloth, then it appears, and comes out from the pores like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it cut, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the lower part down to the upper part, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the tear;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the skin around it, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and put on the oiled wool soaked in egg white;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread comes loose with the skin, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is restrained by the skin on all sides with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows great affliction, pierce it with a subtle needle that goes deep into the eye, and drain the white moisture and lower the eye, and put it back in place immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the swelling of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease, called "alcunnati," is nothing but a swelling gathered in the eye, resembling a descending drop, and it is not actually a drop;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the method of working is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it until you see the swelling come up towards your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it should be fixed, and not descend, and the light should be cleared, and the patient should see things as he used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend from underneath, know that it is a drop, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make a small cut on the cornea along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it has come out, then distil warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then it should be treated with further treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the drops of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have already described the characteristics of the drops in the division, and what is necessary to pierce them;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	then work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You should make the sick person sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the point of the instrument beside the crown, the thickness of a finger, in that white part of the eye near the lower tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and the measurement of the almagda's path should be to the depth of the space between the pupil and the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	then you will see the bone in that parchment, through the clarity of the cornea, and you can place the instrument to the place where the point is, then press it along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the point descends now, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a short rest, and if the point ascends the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and it does not ascend, then extract the almagda gently by turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a little bit of gem-salt on the point, and lift that out of the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply over the eye bandages or wool soaked in rose oil and abundant egg white, and bandage with the sound eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on a compress with abundant egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are such people with excessively hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then put the almagda in, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and for the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which he will sleep on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free from all movements, and let him eat light foods, and do not move his head either to the right or to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see certain things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not appropriate for you to do this during the hour of treatment or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary that you delay this, because the inflammation rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if suppurating abscesses occur, untie the bandages before the seventh day, and use those things which relieve the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it has calmed down, unbind the eye and place a bandage over his face for a few days, and let him remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then gradually leave the room, and return to his normal activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no student should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And a man from Iraq came to us, who told us that in his country, people made a device for collecting water, but I have never seen one in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the shapes of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their heads should be of the same fineness, and the rear in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there are various added fleshy growths on the nose, some resembling scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and in some there is deeply sunken flesh of a dark color, and there is soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that soft flesh, which is not sunken, you must place the patient between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and apply the lancet to that flesh, and draw it out;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then cut off what you can hold with the sharp, thin blade of a lancet, until you know that flesh is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if any remains that cannot be cut, then treat it carefully with all the subtle instruments, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without overcoming it, or an abscess is present, then treat it as necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is a malignant abscess, then hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then apply a mild and sharp vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the poultice works, and moisture comes out as far as the palate, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh growing on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you should insert a rather thick linen thread, and tie it in knots, with a space of a finger or less between each knot;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and have the patient pull the thread end in their nose as hard as they can, and pull it gently until it comes through the nose and into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wishes to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the end that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other until the knots of the thread are close together.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted the flesh, then pull the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has eaten away all remaining flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put a lead foil in the nose for a few days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for cleaning the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit likewise;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a sickness called "telul" arises at the head of the nose, and grows and becomes large often, so that it is a visible thing to look at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore you must cut it at the beginning, and remove it completely, then apply the cautery or burning medicine to the place;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, of poor smell:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if it is not touched with iron, for it is a festering abscess, for when it is cut sometimes, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be cut completely, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is then necessary, when this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh and full of blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips with a suture, then treat it until it is healed;
