et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on either side, you must cauterize all the parts of their core until they bleed, then join the two lips with a suture, tighten it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and crushed frankincense over it;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place a piece of strong or other bonding plaster over the powders, and leave it until it dries on its own, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of the suture is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Hard abscesses occur in the lips of men, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then you must turn the lips, and cut on each side, and take it with forceps and cut it in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then fill the space after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then lift away the pus, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	If so, you must hold it with pliers, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the area ground vitriol, or other constricting and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this happens many times, cut it a second time, and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of saws
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gatherings at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and worm-eaten, such that the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	So you must make the patient sit between your hands, and their head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scabs where they appear until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus do the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other blemishes, until they are cleansed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is there at the first application, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then start again on the second and third day, until you have completely scraped;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the craftsman demonstrates, because the scrapers used to scrape the teeth have different shapes than those used to scrape between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary, when treating a toothache, that you delay extracting it as long as possible, for this should not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a substance very high up until there is no longer any excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to extract it, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have a good tooth extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad extraction, for we have already wanted to do it to these lords;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain of the aching tooth, you must cauterize around the tooth thoroughly in all places to protect the gums from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Then move it with your fingers or subtle pliers in small, careful movements, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the pliers;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, extract the tooth straight without breaking it; and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with lint where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and hold it gently with pliers so it does not break while being pulled;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, and leave a part, and cause the patient greater pain than the first due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not do as ignorant masters do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw and do not bring about what we have recounted;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause great illness through the remaining roots or by breaking the jaw, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or vinegar and oil;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that is not sufficient, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, with which one first moves the teeth, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be of good, strong iron, and they should be toothed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains when pulling, you must put softened cotton soaked in butter for one or two days, so the area softens, then insert the pliers, called "algefri," whose head resembles a bird's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be filed like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, you must expose the flesh all around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", which is to say a pick, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, use all the instruments, of which the shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument that has two blades, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front, in the proportion of the teeth, and of this tool that resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong, so that they cannot break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise, skillful master finds his own instrument, according to what his work and the illness shows him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others; and if one breaks the chariot or other bones, or if it were possible, then he seeks the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and assists with the gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but he can hold and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with suitable medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then remove it with this entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in maiden women, you must know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed:
adonques lou raie;	Then remove it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is air with the tooth, then take this instrument, of which here is the form, and it is similar to a small beak, and is of sharp, tempered iron at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file of this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like the file with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and file the tooth little by little over several days gently, so that it does not move as much as it breaks;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then, finally, smooth it with a rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor spoil the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth loosen, either through impact or falling, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without them falling out, and you have treated them with binding medicines, and this is of no use;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then they must be bound with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there are one or more, until you have carefully reached the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then repeat the covering until the part where you began, and gently and carefully tighten your hand until it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and join them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and position them so that they do not hurt the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it stays, and will serve thus for the entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the manner of straightening the two healthy teeth, and the two misaligned ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, one resets it in its place, little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no one should interfere who is not skilled and patient, and sometimes one makes a tooth shape from cow bone, and places it where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, so that one is born this way;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident from a stitched wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth, and hold their head in your grip, and lift their tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nervous ligament broadly, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment; and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from a stitched wound, then put the hook in and cut that ligament broadly;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the slit is not too deep, for the artery that is beneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift the place with rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then put a linen tent under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and treat the patient each night, so that the place may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, then put powdered vitriol on the place;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it with a lentil cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it as a different color, or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining to suppuration, and there is moisture, then one should apply the lancet, and slit it with a fine spatula, and release it on one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood overwhelms your work, then place powdered vitriol on it until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have extracted all the fluid;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the area with oil and vinegar, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes boils appear in the throat, called "godath," and properly called the two almonds.  And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be warned:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the discharge of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will break open on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is white, pale, and the root is slender, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first observe if the abscess is warm, resting, and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your care, and let the operator open his mouth and take the tongue between his hands, and press the tongue down from the instrument, which has this shape;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of thin silver or bronze, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the forceps and place it in the swelling, and pull it firmly upwards as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull out any matter from the tissues with it, then cut it with the instrument, which has this shape, that resembles a pair of shears;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and nevertheless the tips are curved, and one towards the other, and are very sharp, and are made of hardened or tempered steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, cut it with pliers, which have this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And one side is sharp, and the other is not;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, the patient should gargle with hot, sharp, and easy-to-use water, and if blood comes out, the patient should gargle with water, or boiled pomegranate rind, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them likewise as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed within her throat, that is to say, a small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that it had pushed out two ribs through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then quickly, and inserted a lancet into one, then pulled it out, and extracted a large portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards I inserted the lancet into these abscesses, and cut a part of them out, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began now to drink water, and then wine, and I did not cease to cut away at this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess grew again, and filled the space that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I incised and cauterized it within the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from these matters, and I know not what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is beneath, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the inflamed abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round, gathered, and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if it is bloody or of a dusky colour or black, you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have described, by its colour and length, you must have the patient sit in the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then one should insert the hook into the uvula, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut more than the excess beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, you harm the voice and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said regarding the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, you should use a method to alleviate the fear of the cutting.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And have the patient place their head in your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with a hot sharp iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and fill the end of this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have a small container at the head, where medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the sore;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus drip from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not go down into the throat, and to the wound;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the sore for the amount of half an hour, until you see it is healed and the stinging of the medicine is calmed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton on the sore, until the cotton dries on the sore;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry, and it will fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to reapply the cautery with the medicine, reapply it, and after the cautery, wipe around the sore with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is more effective than the incision, than the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take camomile and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and yarrow and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put some water in it, and bring it to a boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument shaped in this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be made of silver or copper, and let one of its ends be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the ulcer through the pipe, until the ulcer is dead;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After that, repeat often, until the ulcer dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, for many things can happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this fumigation except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a pipe and put a piece of egg white inside one end, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg white does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and that is a good and safe treatment altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the entire instrument, so that you see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps the foreign object will be expelled by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and ties a thread to the sponge and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it reaches the place, it will harden, and then you will pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole thing come off, or push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, so that he knows where the thing is situated;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if he pushes it down, or pulls it out with the entire instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the leech of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the leech is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the sick person in the sun, and then you press his tongue with the instrument I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, then pull it out with a small hook, or with delicate pliers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a thin, braided rope, and put it into the throat of the sick person, and then put a hot iron on the braided rope's end, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the sick person sweats with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand frequently;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall off as we have said, then fumigate the sick person with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have described in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will fall off without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are burning coals, and the bottom is covered with a pierced cover, and in that hole is the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then pour your fumigation into it, and the patient should put the head of the tube in their mouth, and close the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes down to the leech;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the leech will now fall off, and if it does not fall off, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary for it to come out forcefully by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which the leech is drawn out, if one can see it, is like curved pliers, in order to enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a bird, and has the roughness of a file, so that what it takes hold of, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many types of abscesses are described, according to what is remembered from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways, one in its own appearance, and in what it holds of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of fleshy areas differ from those that arise in joints, and each has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the swelling is ripe according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are some that must be pierced when they are swollen and do not ripen according to their completion, like abscesses that are beside joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess arises beside joints, and it is left until it is rotten around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	If the abscess is near the main limb, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the foundation, one pierces it before it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and you should not pierce a swollen abscess without complete digestion, except for one near the foundation, lest it rot deeply, become elongated inside, and form a fistula;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time for the perforation of a ripe abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the calming and sharpening of the abscess's head, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you should place the perforation in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears movable;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be along the body's length, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, and arteries, and in all such places equally where there is no pleura.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the perforation wait until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom will be elongated from it, and is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps the lips and the depth of it harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary to administer small abscesses, small punctures;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many fissures according to the likeness of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the core, and to cut;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become like a flap, and is decayed, then it is necessary to do as one does to boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and some are split into three angles, and some are cut like myrtle leaves, like abscesses of the armpits;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, you should not remove all the pus at that time, but only a portion;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then bandage the abscess until the next day, then remove some more pus again;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this repeatedly, gradually, until all the pus is out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps with the expulsion of the pus, so that the patient, perhaps, dies, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, conduct this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound and examine whether the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a deep wound, apply bandages of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you place a bandage in each one so that they meet each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a portion of skin, and you have trimmed it around, you must fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it for up to three days;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and ease, and moisten a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and remedies, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is in winter, and the area where the abscess is is very sensitive, you must place over it bandages and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, you must place over it cloths moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, for up to three days, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess, dry it and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is necessary to know universally in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	or I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head's tissues come small abscesses, and are kinds of us that are in webs, like the yolks of an egg, and many of similar types.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	Some are fatty and such where there is moisture like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and some are hard and stony when cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is that you must try with every instrument that is called "entromissoire," from which the form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, you cut through it with a long incision.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is emptied, you must then scrape away without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it often returns if you leave any.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	Otherwise, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and that which remains from the night will then heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are certain that it does not remain overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess contains a thick pus, cut it along this length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and drain its pus, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to drawing out the pus where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery is causing resistance, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with a stony abscess, and in cutting and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into a stony and moist abscess is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses are on the head, where there is no moisture, and from these were the abscesses that I cut on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it with anything, one would have inflicted a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses appearing on the head, except those on the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place to allow the pus to come out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofulous abscess is properly within its own pocket, just like a boil and abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that one, then, that you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves on every side, and is not inflamed around the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is necessary to cut it open, and scrape it from every part, and spread the two lips of the wound with forceps, if you need them, as we have said about abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and draw it out little by little, and be certain that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula be neither sharp nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and this prevents you from working, then put powdered vitriol, or some powders that stop blood, into the wound, and constrict the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has stopped, return to your work until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then search with your index finger if any small sores remain, and cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the sore, it is not right to cut that sore at its root, but tie a strong double thread to it, and let it fall off without harming it;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire sore, you must bring together the two edges of the wound and stitch them now, since no excess remains because of the sore's size.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if you must, cut the root, and pull out the pus, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those sores that have excess, pierce them where they appear ripe;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them thus, as the one previously mentioned, by depending from it, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the sore throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with quinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat, called the "epiglottis," be released;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and no aid be given by them, because all the veins and the flesh of the sick person are close to those with a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three or four circles, a small incision through the middle, between the two circles or with the depth of the slit, and not into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and that place is suitable for the incision of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are distant.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, he must stretch the skin of the throat with all his might, then cut the throat until he reaches the channel;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and drain the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the channel that leaps out through the broken place, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the time has passed that one fears strangulation, bring together the two edges of the throat wound, and stitch it all together without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the breathing fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one cuts the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch the wound and heal it, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a lady took a knife and plunged it into her throat, and cut a portion of the throat's flesh.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and saw clearly that she had not cut a vein or artery except the throat, and air was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the lady suffered only that she was hoarse-voiced, and later returned to her normal state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore, I say that there should be no fear in the cutting of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "goiter", and is a large abscess the colour of a jaundice, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where natural has no contrivance.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from us from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and if there is fear, one should not operate forcefully except in the small, and should test and seek throughout the entirety of the injury:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like fat, and it does not connect to any vein, cut it, as one cuts fat, and pull it out from its entire covering, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and thoroughly investigate everything, and treat it as necessary, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of fat
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many types of fat exist, of which I will describe all the varieties;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and here it is necessary for me to say the whole difference that exists between fat and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that issue is hot and feverish, as long as the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Fat has neither heat, fever, nor pain, and contains its own sack, and is similar in color to the body, and begins like a rind, and grows large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the fat, to first examine it with the entire instrument called "entromissoire," according to what its form will be in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of examining abscesses of fat is to take the moistest spot you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, and this is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the instrument, and pay attention to what may jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist matter runs out, whatever color it has, then you lance it as I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if, after the instrument, no moisture comes out, know that it is greasy, then lance it in a cross, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it from each side, and watch the skin where it lies, that you pull it out healthy with the fat;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pus returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains, and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and constrict the wound, and apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the pus is large, then suture the two edges of the wound, and cure it with what generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the throbbing vein is against you or something else, then hurry and fill the place with pulverized vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, until the wound rots and the blood's boiling subsides;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cauterize what has remained of the pus.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the intruding instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and of them there are three squares called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and of them there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, for searching abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles with which one sews garments, and are of brass, or iron, or silver, and better are those that are yellow, and are more proven of black lead for searching the corners of fistulas;
et sont de III manieres:	and are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the probes are of many appearances, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are probes that have two bends of three kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are probes that have three bends, and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are probes that have two bends, and probes of one bend only, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these which are cut are sharp, and of such there are some that do not cut much more than on one side, so that one scrapes the flesh, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these instruments are lancets fitted into handles, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them much except in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and the groin, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to the bark of hazelnuts, according to this shape, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it sometimes at the place that bleeds from cuts in the veins, and arteries, and sometimes according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to become corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to this shape of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as happens with women, then split it into two ribs above, by two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this shape, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and administer to it what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it eats away the remaining and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are a kind of hard scrofulas, where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those, therefore, that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar nature to scrofulas, cut it as we have said in the division of scrofulas, and if the wound returns pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is sealed over it, there often arises an abscess, and likewise it happens to a swollen vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one recognizes it as being due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the tightening.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to the vein, the redness is apparent.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid iron treatment, and the one at the head should also be avoided, and in that which is swollen from an artery, one must cut through the skin from the length.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then make the incision with a scalpel, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed.
