puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then place a needle underneath it, and pierce it through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then pierce the place between the two ligatures with a lancet until the blood flows out and the abscess is relieved.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the treatment that causes the swelling to subside, until the ligature falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with the appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is due to a vein incision, you must hold as much of the abscess as possible on your hand, then insert a needle under the area you hold, pierce it, and apply a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligature on one of the two sides, using the two ends of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you fear the thread will loosen, re-insert another needle through the entire thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess from the core and leave what is attached.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer treatments of poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come to the arteries and veins, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often to the shoulders and arms and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various conditions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is squeezed tightly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it moves well in every direction, and neither forward nor backward, nor beneath nor above, and that which is in joints should not be cut with a knife.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	Perhaps contraction would result.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And that which is on the head or forehead, pierce the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with a hook, and scrape it, then remove it and stitch the wound together and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in the belly and nowhere else, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is subtle, and the stem large.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are small and very large ones.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference; they were white, had fine roots, were often split, and moisture often ran from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found eighteen ounces in one, and six in the other; the procedure for the incision is that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If it is cut with a wide spatula, and the cautery iron is in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in the cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, then take a well-made lead thread and tie the tumor as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	And then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the lead thread until it cuts through the tumor, and it breaks apart without effort;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	And if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting, especially for the belly, but you may well cut half of it and then cauterize it so it does not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tumor which is of fixed color and poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the abscess is mature
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the abscess comes from a wound or a cut, and is on the abdomen, and some of the abscesses arise, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries as described before, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from the rupture of the skin and the discharge of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, and appears with diverse discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with the fingers it recedes, and then returns, and perhaps it is sealed, and grows greatly at the entrance to the bath and because of hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and appears clearly when you press it with your hand, and does not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you should leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or bowels, you should instruct the patient to hold their breath and lie stretched out straight, then apply leeches all around the wound;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then have him lie often between your hands, then go around the area that you have marked with leeches, then spread half the abscess over the entire large incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the wound be free from the binding;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the half of the abscess spread over the binding, and place your index finger into it, and seek the intestines;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the binding, then untie it, and push the intestine to the outside of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, then take it to the incision, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein hinders you, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads into them, and put the two needles around what you have made in a cross that you made pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then constrict the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until it rots, and the dead flesh falls away by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is softened and rotten, then treat it with what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area with what is necessary, and close the area.
dou chancre	of chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have discussed in the division the appearances of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicine, and how one should avoid the treatment with iron;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that chancre develops in the flesh, and great care is needed in the treatment, and the ancients said that when chancre is in a place where one can scrape it off, like chancre in the breasts, and in the thigh, and similar places, and it should be entirely removed when it is in the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you should not approach it, for I have never cured any such;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	No one ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then let the patient bleed if there is a manifest fullness, then prepare the patient well for the treatment;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then remove your instruments from the ulcer, and shave the hair from all sides, and remove the bone from all sides, leaving nothing;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and thoroughly clean the area with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding is too much and it is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already discussed the different types of dropsy, how the accumulation of water happens, the signs of each type, and the treatments using medicine and those using iron:
si est eclites soulement;	if it is just a simple case;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not use iron in these two types:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	namely, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy called "eclites" with medicine, and the treatment does not help, check if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as diarrhea, constipation, or similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	then do not use iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see a patient with strong constitution, and they have only dropsy as an illness, and are not too young or too old, then you should act like this:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient straight onto your hands, and apply pressure to the belly by pushing the water towards the lowest part of the chest, then take the thorny spatumile according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	pointed, and yet not so penetrating that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot wound them;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then observe if the dropsy is lodged towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if this is so, you must cut open above the pouch three straight incisions below the blade;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to a liver ailment, let your incision be on the left side of the pouch, three inches;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to the spleen, let it be on the right; and it is not appropriate for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to that weak spot;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce through all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand through all the space between the skin and the surface, just as in skinning, to the depth of a fingernail or a little more;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the surface until the space reaches the empty place, and that is the place of the water, then draw it out, and put in this instrument of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is of bronze or light iron, and has a small hole on the underside;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision by which the writer shapes the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of the head is the groove, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it will now descend onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient will die because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the disposition of the patient's virtue and pulse signify;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then draw the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the heart that seals the opening on the surface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then recommence the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering this, and draw a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and beware of failing until there remains only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave a lot of water there, then cure it with hot sand or burial, and by sweating a lot or bathing and sunbathing, and let him drink;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and cure it with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it must be pierced, then it should be pierced very subtly in this shape.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then place a subtle lead plug in the opening, and bind it and keep it thus for three or four days.  And when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then replace it.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes to flow will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose opening is small shall be treated with a lead plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate unless they raise their penis.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the bladder, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the method of treatment is that the patient lies often on their back, then extends the head of the penis and cuts it like the shank of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as is necessary;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the sores on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times these sores appear on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and some are malignant and some are not;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if it is necessary to take them with a fine forceps, and cut and clean them all, then put on moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the sore is malignant, of foul color and stinking, then you should apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and if the sore is under the shaft, and part of it is within the skin and part outside, then you should remove the part of the sore that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is closed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat them together, the shaft of the penis is not certain to not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come to the penis and to the testicles;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	So it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and figs, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cauteries help with two conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, to the bleeding, and to the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	And if the shaft of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you should insert a lead pipe into the penis, and the patient should urinate through it;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And when the skin is inflamed on the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to a wound or abscess, then you must cauterize it with a heated instrument, until the connection is severed, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if it is a serious condition, you should cauterize a small area on the head of the penis and the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then gently separate them and place a thin linen bandage soaked in cold water on it, so it does not become inflamed again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a simple severing like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, when we perform this operation, especially on children, it is necessary to do the best and most gentle work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not prescribe circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their laws, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen most of the masters and lords who performed circumcision using a knife, or force, or some new tool;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If the knife slipped, because there are two blades, and perhaps one above is cut and the one below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Then it must be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and the healing of the knife wound is not certain on the tip of the limb;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and during the healing of the nail, perhaps the iron escapes, and the work is undone, and many times they heal without needing more healing, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the healing done with force, and with a thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for force cuts evenly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, you cut evenly throughout all the time.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but let the thread be tight around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first work is such that you should make the child, if he understands, think that you are only tying the thread around the rod, and you can make him happy in all the ways you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then hold it upright between your hands, and hold the forces between your hands or under your feet so the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then place your hand on the rod and blow into the core, and pull it upwards until the head of the rod is straight.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then cleanse it well of the dirt that has collected there, then tie the marked spot with a double thread, then tie it under one stitch to the other.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with your two fingers by the second stitch, the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two stitches, then lift the core quickly and pull the head of the rod.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then allow the blood to run drop by drop, for this is the cure.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder over and over the powder, a thin layer of glue made from a boiled egg diluted with rosewater, mixed with good, fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces for cleansing is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two heads should be taut and sharp, and the heads should also be as large as the handle equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error in the cleansing occurs when the heart is exposed within the incision.
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Then you should extend it to your fingernail, lest the place become an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your fingernail, then hold it with pliers and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pass three days, and that which is beneath the rod is swollen, leave it until the hot abscess is calmed, and lightly scrape it.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	Cut it as best you can, and be careful not to harm the part of the rod, this will not hurt it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Then treat the place with the things suited to wounds, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if one cuts deeper than necessary and it goes above, it will not be harmful.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is caused by a blockage of stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released, and you see the retention to be caused by a stone that is lodged in the neck or the bladder, then the patient should be bent over their knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And the feet should be placed on the back, and the patient should extend their abdomen toward the back, and the patient should restrain their breathing as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with the instrument called a "syringe," of which this is the shape:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it should be of fine, light silver, like the feather of a bird.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And it should be one and a half palms long, and thin at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of releasing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton to the end, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the excess wool and push it to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a stool, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently place the syringe on the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then pull the penis up towards the groin;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and the patient feels it coming to the empty space, and this is not done in this order except because the passage it goes through is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then pull out the thread with the small piece of wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and make the urine flow;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you wish to distill sharp things and medicines there, then use the instrument that is called a "clepsydra," and this is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and has three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the channels through which the medicine flows should be such that they tightly seal the urethra without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and inject when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you wish to inject your medicines into the bladder, place the tip of the injector into the moisture, and pull while injecting;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	so you will draw the moisture into the injector, and then push the injector forcefully in;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	so the moisture will enter, and will go to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and that is the form of the subtle clyster used to clyster the bladder:
si est ci:	if it is so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	and it is of silver or of metal, and the tip is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and underneath the skin where the vein falls;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it with which you wish to clyster the bladder, then tie it between the two skins with a double linen thread, and heat the moisture a little over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the tip of the clyster into the tube, then squeeze your hand over the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has arrived in the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dial, and put inside it what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you did with the bladder, squeezing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already discussed in the division the types of stones, and their extraction along with the medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and have described the difference between stones in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stones one should operate with a scalpel;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that stones lodged in the bladder happen more often to children, and this is a sign that water leaks from the bladder, similar to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it shows sand, and the patient rubs their penis, and it hangs down many times, and then hardens;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and much of this leaking damages the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the healing is easy in children up to four years old, and is very difficult in old people, and is moderate in young people, those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the waste that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and raise and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from the upper part;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then have him sit between your prepared hands, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is all sloping downwards;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then search for and touch it inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall out upon touching at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a young adult.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and place it in his/her fundament, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on your finger, and push it out to the place where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his/her hand, and command him/her to extend the nipples upward with his/her right hand, and with his/her left hand remove the skin beneath the nipples in the area where the incision is to be made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then insert the spatula, the shape of which is this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And cut between what is between the nipples and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left groin;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight over the stone, and your fingers be continually on the fundament, and let the cut be through so that it is wide outward, and narrow inward, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	perhaps the pressure from your finger on the fundament will cause it to jump outward without difficulty;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are stones that have angles and edges:
si est griés a issir;	if it is difficult to remove;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and there are some that are smooth, similar to a ball, and round, from which the removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it doesn't come out, you must use tongs, which are like a file at the end, to hold and pull the stone so it doesn't slip away;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you place beneath it a thin, curved instrument at the end;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot extract it thus, enlarge the opening a little, and if the blood flows, staunch it with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, first take out the largest one, and then cut above it, and pull it out forcefully, and then the smaller ones if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be loosened, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where he dies, or his urine comes out repeatedly through the wound because the place cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nonetheless, try to pull it out, or break it with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and compress it, and place over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then bind the patient's neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealings of blood in the bladder, and the urine is retained thereby, which is known in such a manner that without discharge with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and rot it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then clean the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and assist him in every way you know, until he is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind his two thighs together, and assemble the remedies over the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and is stuck in, and the urine cannot exit;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if you treat it as I have previously said, that you cut it many times, one is excused from the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this shape and let it have three angles placed in a triangle.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then gently insert the drill into the urethra until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the drill in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then urine will come quickly, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then it will be broken, and will jump out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then cut the urethra at the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	Sometimes a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-skilled who will expose herself to scrutiny, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-skilled in this art of medicine;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth way is that the stone in the woman is deeper than the stone in the man, so that a deeper incision is needed, and there is great fear. And if necessity commands this, you must take a skilled midwife, and it is hard to find one, and if you find none, search for a subtle and chaste mirror;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present a wise and experienced woman, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to perform what you order her to do in the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and observe closely whether the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must insert her finger into the fundament and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she must hold it beneath her finger, and instruct her to insert her finger into the afflicted area, and seek it pressing her left hand firmly against the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh, opposite the middle of the groin, where it is apparently located, and feel the stone in that area;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move her finger over or under the stone, and let the incision be small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the instrument into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound until the stone can come out forcefully, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	so know their appearances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the blood overcomes you, put powdered vitriol in the place, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have instruments as I have told you in the extraction of stones, to help you in your task;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and bind it with bandages, and do not begin again this, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient die;
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided, and the place is healed, then return to your task, until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	A watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white pus beneath the skin of the testicles, which contains the egg;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "pus", and sometimes it is properly within the sac of the testicle, so that one might think it another egg;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin of the testicle between the white pus that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this happens rarely.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is a color leaning toward jaundice, or it is blood red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs for knowing this assembly, because if it is the white, as we have said, then it is a deep abscess, a little long like the shape of an egg, and the testicle is not apparent, because it is surrounded by moisture entirely.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in its own fabric, then the abscess is deep with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white surface, one feels it well.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you test it throughout the inner space, the form of which is mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the inner space, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be made healthy according to their power and the fullness of their body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then support him on his back, on a somewhat raised surface, and place many cloths under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the testicles lengthwise through the middle, right up to the point of the knife, and make your incision perfectly straight, dividing the skin of the testicles down to the white surface, and carefully peel it back according to your ability;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the flat surface with water through one large opening, and draw out all the water, and then place your hooks, and stretch the surface upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the testicles themselves, but only the surface;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or in pieces very subtly, the side of it, if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the testicle jumps out during your work, put it back in place once you have finished working on the surface;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then stitch together the two leathers of the testicles with a stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another illness, you must tie the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the flow of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the testicle with the entire suspensory, remove the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the bone is joined in two parts together, know that these are two splinters;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then cut the other part in the same way as you did the first, then wipe the blood away, and put moistened wool in rose oil on the wound;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another layer of wool soaked in wine and oil over the two splinters, and place doubled cloths on top, and bandage it according to this method:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool in this manner and sew them together at the crotch of the breeches, and one end goes over the bottom to the back, and the other to the area around the groin;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two ends over the two armpits, and the entire fastening should be gathered at the buckle of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this wound is treated with cautery instead of cutting with iron, and you should take a sharp surgical cautery iron, and cut the skin over the splinters, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing the liquid is exposed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	then take the cautery according to this method, and pierce that surface with the prongs, and scorch it with this hot, sharp cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut it in every way that you can, until you remove everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and be careful that the fire does not touch the testicle;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more healing;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and carefully avoiding blood flow, and gentler than the work of cutting;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything opposes you, whether an abscess or blood flow or something else, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then perform perforation, as I have told you, and if you are certain, through the signs we've discussed, that the watery humor is superficial, then have the patient sit on a raised seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the part beneath the entire skin surface, and place the perforation lengthwise along the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the opening be wide, so that all the fluid drains out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the area, and bind it, and allow the remaining fluid to drain, and then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the fluid to escape from the opening of the wound, then you must insert a reed or an instrument used to extract fluid from hydrops, of which the form is previously described;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the fluid returns, and is collected after six months or more, and when it is collected as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this ailment there is fear in several dispositions, wherefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the treatment and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come upon the body, and especially on the testicles;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to say by a superfluity of sharp and acute [humor], which is spread to the testicles, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and finds no pain, and is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and perhaps an abscess is grievous, fearful and painful, and of a dark color, and sometimes comes from a cut artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a cut artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	One that is made from the swelling of a vein is known by its disposition to the pressure of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this type, and on other sores;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And it is that you cut the core of the testicles, then lift the testicle upward, and pull the white membrane firmly, and free the suspensory ligament from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the testicle is already swollen with these related sores, then you must pull the testicle and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is airy on the surface, or in that which is inside the vessels, then you must free all that membrane, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the sore is in the rear, then you must cut it all, and extract the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping resembling a boil, with a softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this illness is as dangerous as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you its method, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You must have the patient sit upright, then place the suspensory for the testicles down to your fingers, covering all the vessels near the penis, and the master should grasp them and extend them firmly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then, with a sharp, wide scalpel, cut across the vessels, until they are exposed, and then cauterize each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the wound appeared, and tie it again to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut them in the middle directly, along the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as the others, where pus is generated, so that no vessels leak to nourish one of the testicles.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For by this there is no harm, and if blood comes from all the vessels, then both testicles should be removed.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the surface
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this wound is due to the cut or tear in the surface, or the stretching on the belly in the area of the groin, so that the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this rupture is either in the surface, or from its stretching, and these two types come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from a blow, or a fall, or a strain, or the lifting of a heavy load, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the stretching of the surface are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are even up to almost the bottom, because the surface presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is from the section of the surface are that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear various, beneath the skin, and this is due to the escape of the intestines and the body escaping from the surface.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the hernia, and are trapped within, and cause great suffering to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with fear, because it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of the work is that you instruct the patient to return the intestine with his hand into the wound, if it can be returned;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be placed back on his neck, between your hands, and lift the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the torso upwards, and cut all the skin from the testicles lengthwise;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push inside the lips of the waist, with hooks as you need to open the wound, and be such that the pus can come out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the surface that is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white surface is exposed on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your index finger into that which surrounds the testicle, into that which is between the white surface that is under the skin of the testicle, and the second surface, and separate that which is behind the testicle, and between the second surface;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move the right hand inside the body of the testicles, and extend the white surface upwards with your left hand, and lift the testicle with all its surface towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the attendant to extend the testicle upwards, and loosen that which is above behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around the hard white surface, and if you find anything, place it into the abdomen below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of X threads, and place it in the rear part of the surface, which is after the skin of the testicles;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the ends that appear of the threads, until there are four threads;
