puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one over the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the surface, of which we have spoken, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the ends of the threads, and bind them firmly in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter, so that a festering abscess does not arise;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put back the bandage according to the first bandage, long two fingers of that, and after these two bandages, leave of the surface, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, the width of one finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other, according to the roundness that the egg bears;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part that is beneath the skin of the testicles, as much as the blood runs, and the swelling, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool soaked in oil, and put on wounds, and administer the bandage that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white surface that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to the fear of blood flowing.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the bandage until it falls off by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it takes too long to fall off, it should be soaked with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls off;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this treatise, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done as in the treatise which is next to the text, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting slightly above or below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut it in half, and treat the abscess of that which opens, until the vessel drains;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture occurs within the ribs, as we have said, and the wound opens;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and no intestines descend into the groin; and if any descend, it is little, and repairs itself at any time;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nonetheless if it stays too long in this place, the wound or ulcer grows, until the intestine descends;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the ulcer that is on the ribs, as we have said, for it extends, then softens and swells the place, and it opens;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is through cautery, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient often lies on their back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflamed with a broad blade according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the ulcer that is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the rod and place it on the apparent place of the ulcer;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it deep into the belly, then cut the two apparent places of the ulcer above the head of the rod, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the rod, and do not cut the ulcer or extend the egg or anything else, as I have shown you in the treatment of the intestines' rupture;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ulcer is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the tissues within are softened, and it is visible.
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that one have the sick person lie on their back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the stitches, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread falls out.
dou chastrement	of the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is only necessary for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the master may be able to answer when asked, and to know the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we do by pulling, we make the animal sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and hanging.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of castration of the tail:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	you must restrain the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each testicle in one blow, once you have properly burned them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no bit of the surface and the subtle surface that is over the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of castration is gentler than that done by pulling, because in pulling, perhaps some part of the testicles remains, causing the animal to desire lust;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two testicles appears also like the form of a woman's nature, or there is hair, and sometimes urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has above the vulva also like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the cure for the man and the woman is that you cut away the joined flesh, and treat them like other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenecide
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentigene is a joined flesh over the natural part, so that it is too ugly to look at;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	You must cut the excess tentigene with your hand or shears, and cut it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deep, lest a flow of blood come, then treat it with another cure until it is healed;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and there is another flesh that arises from the mouth of the wound, and fills it, and perhaps leaps out, and is like a scab, and for this the ancients called it "scab disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary, you must cut it, as we said the tentigene, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is by nature, or by accident through illness that has come to it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by added flesh, or by a thin or thick surface, and is made deep within the marrow, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the ability to have children;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is by the examination of the wound.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the numbness is visibly near, then look at your fingers or the limb.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is from a thin surface, and it is near the two lips, then hurry, and do this:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, with her legs spread apart;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then stretch the two lips widely, until the thin surface is healed, and the numbness is relieved;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman lie on her back every day, so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the surface is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the numbness is of fresh flesh, then suspend it on a hook and cut it.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have medicines that stanch blood, such as dragon's blood, frankincense, and the white of an egg mixed together;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a broad lead band so that the wound cannot heal;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it remain for a long time, and apply a dry linen tent;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be treated with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the flesh there comes a new growth, it must be cut according to this method, if it is not a festering abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For a festering abscess in the flesh, one should not use fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become painful.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have already discussed the similarities to them, and the signs, and I will now discuss those that receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and pain, when deep within the flesh and do not appear on the surface, are not cured by cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the flesh, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cool room, then grasp the pain with pincers, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines that constrict blood, such as oak galls and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if a discharge of blood comes, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a poultice for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without causing wounds;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take wool, and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointments until it is healed;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and the one called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough head, so it should be cut like the thelul I said;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the marrow, such as ulcers and stony abscesses, herpes, blisters, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary, therefore, that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that collect pus;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you wish to know the treatment with iron, observe whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and whether it turns red, if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is relieved;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and let him have two small seats where he can lean, and lean on his back and bring his feet to the sides of the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the wound towards the right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the sore, from which the shape will come afterwards;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, that you first insert the rod to know the depth of the sore, so that what enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the sore with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he place the cone of the instrument on top, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is open, and it is opened by hand gently, then it must be cut at the head, with a sharp instrument.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the boil is emptied, then it is necessary that you place in the wound wet cloths in rose oil, or in dried green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and place the cloth deep within the wound, and place on top of the wound and on top of the lancet clean wool soaked in water or boiled mallows;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it after two days of the appropriate ointment, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes one cleans the wound by means of an enema of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and long-boiled aristolochia;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is festering in the wound, you must avoid cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the nature of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the child hastens to be born.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	Then know that this birth is according to natural form, and the child emerges beneath its head, and the afterbirth with it.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child exits quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	For when it descends under its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	And that which comes out otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it sometimes comes out on its feet, or the body or head, or hands, or it comes out on its belly, or sometimes, and is perhaps turned around on its neck, and by other bad positions.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the positions how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes out on its head through a natural passage, and the woman is giving birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a stool, or have women hold her up.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	And apply oil or fennel seed poultice, and then let the midwife place the small spatula, whose form is like this, between her fingers:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	And cut the afterbirth, and cut with her fingernail until the moisture inside comes out.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	And press the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman an enema of fennel seed and dill seed oil.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Then make her drink and sneeze with the mixture, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Then the child will come out now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands come out forcibly, it is necessary that you gently reposition them little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then lift the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when it is lifted;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed before, and extract the child, and reposition it likewise.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's exit from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, it should be pushed upward;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take it by the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it jumps as far as the thighs, then order it to grab, and make it sneeze by condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps free, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not free as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come free as we have said, take chickweed, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on the affected part of the woman this ointment, and then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened from below, make her a poultice of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will now jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the delivery of the child upon her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes into this form, let the midwife put her hands gently.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then let her be supported on her neck, and her feet hang down, and let her lie on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and gently fold her hands, and then grasp her hands on her stomach, and remove the cushions underneath her, until she is ready to deliver;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not emerge, then grasp her feet and move them forcefully, then move her stomach upwards, then push with your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and draw the child out gently;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and tell the woman to strain as hard as she can until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child who comes out with one hand outstretched
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise a way to bring the hand back.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, have the woman lift and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, have her lie down on the bed, and straighten her legs firmly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the poultice that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a seat, then study to bring the hand back;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and bring the child according to its natural form, and have her sneeze, and instruct her to strain until the child is out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the child's exit on her neck, and let her hands be spread out, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the attendant hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and move it gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, then put on the natural mucous substance of aloe and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, have her sit on the seat, and instruct her to strain;
et la fai esternuer.	and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for the entire afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this manner for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child hangs on its face and on its neck, cut it from the body, so that it is not held back, and the child dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as is proper, and instruct the woman to take herself some rest:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live long, if at all;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the surface which divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they emerge as naturally as one whole child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they emerge with difficulty, the cure is as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and do quickly and lightly what she must;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it deserves to be healed.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to fifteen, and are all formed in the form of a child by the measure of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the midwife know all this, for perhaps such things happen to her;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman of a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to manual work;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister should hold her in two parts, or bind her to the bed so that she is not pulled down by the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with the mucilage of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the hands of the attendant with these oils and mucilages;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently insert them into the womb, then seek the place where she puts the hooks that are appropriate to it, and watch if the child is prepared to descend on its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if place the hooks in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the armpit or near the ribs, and if the descent is on its feet, then place it in the legs and middle ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the hook in his right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and gently insert it with his whole hand, and fix the hook in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert another hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it equally by moving from one side to the other, to pull it out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold it, as is the form here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then anoint some of his fingers with oil, and insert them into that part, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if any part remains, then place this hook in a higher position, and do so until it is entirely removed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and he cannot pull it back due to the tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth, until it is entirely removed;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cut at the joint of the sole or with a knife, and thus you must do in the other hand, and the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and the passage narrow, or it has a sharp point assembled, then you must put a pointed spatula between your fingers, and split the point and remove the sharpness;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus do the same if the child has a large head naturally;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then draw the bones with pliers, and if the head slips out and it is tight with a force, let it be split, until the moisture that is in the pus is released;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the traction is gentle, and the straightening towards the mouth of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrow in the belly or in the breast, you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and split the belly or breast, until the moisture that is there runs out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, the healer puts his hand deep into the wound, and pulls it until the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts one or two hooks in, and pulls it forcefully;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come in, then one should not work on it, but one must administer moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and he administers plasters, and sips in soft and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said about a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot, then pull it forcefully in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said concerning hot abscesses that come in the wound;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a discharge of blood comes, then it should be placed in constricting water, and he should administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had been dead, then another placed above it, and the other was also killed.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared in the groin, and swelled until it opened, and began to discharge greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered it for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-drawing plaster, and one bone came out, and after a few days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I probed the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived a long time like this, and a little bit of pus would come out from the place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter only so that when the master finds a strange thing, he may know how to assist it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marrow back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	After this comes the form of the press, with which the books were made;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and with two turns on two sides of the two chains.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the tube should be one finger wide, and the margin of the wood one finger, and one and a half palms long;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two chains should be two attachments of this same tube, which should be fastened on one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two attachments are put into the mouth of the marris to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to pliers;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have two attachments at the two ends, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you want to open the marris with the whole instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging down and legs open, then put the two joined attachments together into the marris, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand on the whole instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the marris, so that the woman does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all equipped, and their appearances are multiplied;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the master has them prepared, the work is all the faster and the more expensive for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcefully, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps because of this, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, she takes a pot, and makes a hole in the lid, and puts herbs that can open the passage of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then place one end of the cane in the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the womb, and warm it until the vapors enter the womb;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the afterbirth will come out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in oil of sesamum or in the juice of mallow, and then apply it to the area, and seek the afterbirth;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, then she should take it and stretch it slowly and correctly, so that the womb does not rupture during the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it should be moved slightly to the right and to the left, and then pulled.
si venra et se desaerdra.	It will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the womb is too tight, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and the fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not healed by all that we have said, then be careful not to overdo the pulling.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that what is at the opening of the womb, you tie it to the woman's thigh, then administer a clyster of four-ingredient ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it will fester and heal, and come to strength;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	However, when it festers, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore, suitable fumigations are needed for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have proven the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman with the retention of flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is of a similar shape to a chain, and one places the slender end in the natural opening, and the wider ends over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be over the embers, and the scab until it is gone, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but instead have it stopped by a subtle, thin membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	If so, it is then necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not to pierce it with a pointed instrument, and to be careful of the tying so as not to touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place soaked wool in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop up, place a lead chain in the opening and leave it in place for several days, and have it removed when the child is ready to go to the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes these stoppages come from the closing of a wound or abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to cut that blockage;
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is treated, as we have said about the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are lumps, and swellings that come from beside the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or several;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that lump is old, it opens, and often discharges white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are known by this, that there comes out either excrement or flatulence when the sick person expels excrement, and perhaps a worm leaps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach down to the hip joint, and to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the perforating fistula at the fundament, and not the non-perforating one:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you put your index finger into the fundament, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is a twisting, then insert a thin lead tent, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from the opening with expulsion, wind, or pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce;
si te haste dou curer.	therefore hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces down to the bladder or to the urine duct, urine leaks out, and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has pierced down to the hip joint, the tent extends to the spot;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the pain is localized around it, then a boil will often appear there, and no medicine or ointment will help;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these piercing fistulas there is no cure except for labor, and the foolishness of the false healers who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In one that is not piercing and not old, there is hope for health by means of iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of bronze, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you should put your index finger there, and then feel that the tent has pierced it;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be uncovered where you feel between your finger the surface or the flesh, then know that it is piercing;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if not, do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	However, it is said that some can be healed, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that is given is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and puts it, all hot, into the fistula, until it comes near the bottom;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these false tissues are burned, which are like a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with tents soaked in butter, until that tissue comes out, then treat with ointment, causing new tissue to grow and close.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, otherwise cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters, and does not pierce to the finger which is at the foundation, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or pus, and you see the fistula at that which followed the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward, and then cauterize afterward, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be delivered, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then cleanse those misplaced flesh that appear like a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For cauteries of fire bring together two good things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these added flesh, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure it with wet cloths in butter or crushed herbs, until the place yields pus, and the burned flesh issues in the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with ointments, strong and penetrating into hard flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula reaches down to the bottom, and is far from the body, then put your finger in the bottom and explore it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel a membrane, and between it and the tissue or skin, or it is close to piercing, then there is no other way than hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, you place plasters and treat it as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the bottom, and the expulsion occurs against your will.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it, once it is cut away from the base, or with a plaster or another suitable instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse the injured flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then strive to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula on the outside of the base:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	it will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes fistulas are according to this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the base next to the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one thread twisted into two, and put the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is piercing into the margin of the base within, then pull out the thread from that hole, as if you put your finger in the base;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, so that the thread cuts the flesh that is between the two, and it falls;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make the lacing cut so deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatumile spine, with which one opens the fistula, is very sharp on one side and sharp.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and often blood flows from them, and there is one or more of them, and they are under the fundament and at the head of the fundament;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are underneath have little moisture, and often discharge a little of yellowish water or a little blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament is that you instruct the patient to strain himself to go to the privy, until the fundament gives way, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and pull it with pliers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then they are taken with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamelot;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders on top that are in the place of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then give the patient a mordant and harsh clyster to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	If the patient complains, and if the threads are loose from the foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your fingernail or pliers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and that they fear incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	Thus it is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one to run the excess of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place upon the base a damp cloth in rose oil or in cerote, and place upon the base, and instruct the patient that he rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they fall, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the base.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of the bowels in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary, you should scrape the scab off with a spatula or your fingernail, which should not be allowed to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is healed as is appropriate.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, scrape it again more forcefully than before, until it is quite sore and scabbed over.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	then it trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small, false appearance around the body, and goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds cold, and it is felt just as though trembling, and it comes over the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a stick made of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that stick over the trembling, so that the circle surrounds the trembling entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to the entire stick so that you cut around the trembling, and put it deep, and pull the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of brass or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and sharp above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	not pierced, so as to hold it to the finger, and to press it.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you wish, cauterize the trembling, as it is before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or of archaut, or of melted or hammered brass;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which one administers in the treatment of children and those who are weak and sorrowful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is thus wide at the top, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and there be a separation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head be pierced within;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and have two holes on one side, and one on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly, where one puts the medicines, be of an animal bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have one thread of space between each hole, then put one strong thread of twisted thread into each hole in an X or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and that is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or similar thing, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the minister squeezes it with both hands together, until it is all empty, then remove the clyster, and the patient raises their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as it can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer the clyster in a disease of diarrhea, and the medicine is quick to leave, repeat it until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster by which the skin is squeezed:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cutting of swords and knives, or of lances or wood or arrows, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, like a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, so take care if it is from throwing stones or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless broken and the wound is large, and you doubt the rise of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you make it bleed immediately from the cephalic, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the blood flow opposite the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and keep the patient from repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes there, cotton soaked only in rose oil, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been altered by the air, a powder, which I will tell a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has altered it, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together with tents, bring them together by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, of the ribs.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, cut it off;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as roasted meats and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rot in the leather, and it is not reaching the bone, cut out all the rot, and throw it away, then cure it;
