et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then find the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and put this powder in it so that the wound has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take frankincense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living coals three parts, and powder it subtly, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bandage it well, and leave it without untying, if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses only coals, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the burning has not changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burning has changed the wound, especially if it is, then one does not put this powder in it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but puts on some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it produces pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cures it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you afterwards the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference from one of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to let it heal, and put nothing constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is also with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be soaked, like warm wash in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and the decoction also in soft water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce it in a lower place;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding results, then cauterize it, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the passageway is protected, through which food goes, then stitch the heart to the cartilage of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then restrain the swelling, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then dig it out;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and those that you cannot get, then leave them until the wound has festered, and the exit has separated and become clear;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if gases escape from the wound as the patient breathes:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it tightly due to the blood, lest it lingers deep, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to absorb any moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	then there will be no spasm, nor tremor of the heart, nor constriction of the veins;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with bandages and other remedies, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and opens again, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if you treat it as you should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the chest or back, treat it like the wound that is on the front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with stitches;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deeply embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, then treat the wound, and pull out the splinters if they are detached;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not detached, let the wound fester, so the extraction will be easier;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and the judgment for other wounds on other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, so that they get entrapped;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the treatment is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is more difficult to put the intestines back in, if one does not put them back in quickly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they are more difficult to return, and therefore a medium wound is better, because it is easier to return the intestines to their place than in the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common treatments occur in the treatment of the belly, and the treatment of other wounds of the body and two other treatments specific are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more specific to the treatment of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and some thing of the intestines protrudes, and it is difficult to return, it is by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in just warm water, or boil it in water with saffron, and cypress, and spices, and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes use astringent wine, and it is more effective than water alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or cooked mallows and aloes, for by this the entrance to it is eased by little.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then cut the wound a little with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is more effective than the incision, and no one should make an incision without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts within the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, then return it behind according to the natural form into its proper place, if you have the power, for this is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the part beneath the belly, then it is necessary that you make the sick person lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part beneath the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then focus on making the injured part higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, use what is appropriate, then have in your hands a skillful physician who holds the entire rupture in their hand, and brings the edges together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and that is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the size of the wound, then leave a space of one inch from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the underlying skin, until you have pierced through that part, and join the two edges of the underlying skin together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, then join the two edges of the wound together, and then leave one inch of space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this, according to what you need for the needles, until the whole wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium, between fine and thick, for fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore, they must be medium;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and you must not push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and widen the wound before it is closed;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the points of the needles, so they do not injure the patient while they sleep, and put threads or bandages on the points of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one or two needles are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method is common, and is that you join the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh together with one needle and a strong, medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four edges together, then draw the needle back to the starting point, in the manner in which one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the size of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This method is known to men, and I sewed a wound a man had in his belly, which had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and intestines were protruding about two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sewn up within fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I did not treat it with any ointment, because I was in a place where no ointments or other medicines were found.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I would place old cotton over the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and bring it out from the outside to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the heart of the right in the right, then leave the tip of the thread or the stitching where you put the needle, and pierce it again from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furriers sew furs, and that you leave the thread one time on one side, and take it again on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is as some do, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Place a needle at the near end of the thread, and pierce only that spot, and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside to the inside, at the two ends of the thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce each from the outside to the inside, at two other ends of the thread that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the best and most common manner of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen said this, and some bear witness, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the burning has changed it, you return the intestine to its place and sew it up;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on powdered, healing flesh, and if the burning has changed it, put on any ointment that is available, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And stitch the threads, and let the suture and the bandage be bound.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, then as soon as it begins to heal, put on old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in addition, when the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound might spread to the main limbs, then you should soak light wool in tempered oil, or rose oil, and put it around the joints, and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if it feels pain or rot in the boils, and this often happens, then irrigate them with heated dark wine, especially if the rot reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded, and this is due to the network of veins in it, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the hernia jumps out of the wound, replace it just like the intestine, while it's fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and turned dark or black, you must tie the dark area to prevent blood from flowing, for there are veins and arteries there.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two ends of the part below the wound out, so as to ease the extraction when the hernia falls, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the abdomen.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is wounded, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became chronic and turned into a fistula, and waste and gas were discharged from it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and I did not cease to apply remedies until it was healed, and the area was joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healed, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a strip of strong fabric, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the strip has opened its mouth, place it over the two edges so that it firmly closes over them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the strip's end, and this stays in place so it cannot come undone, then place another strip in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This method works on the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestines with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine, in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestinal thread, which should be very thin, and then tie a thin linen thread to the end of the thread, then put the thread in the needle and sew the intestine, and bring it back together to repair the tear;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing with strips is nothing more than following the path of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill or remedy, but only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it has lingered, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is festering and filled with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula, in truth, is a hard and white knotted swelling, where no pain is felt, and is also festering like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear pus, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times quite large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is not caused by anything except one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or the body;
ou por sa malice;	or by its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is rotten, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow to digest, and delays recovery, and swells by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I make you know the cure of the fistula which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula happens in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the surface, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some come to the property of the principal limb, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have confidence in its cure, and you wish to know it, then take a tin or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, then seek it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then seek it with a thin lead tent, for lead bends easily around the crookedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well seek it with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will run from one opening to another, and clean it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then seek it wisely to your power, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and is deep inside, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the corruption and the corrupted flesh that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, you must cut deep, as much as you can, then place moistened tents in a sharp medicine, and put them down to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply ointments that promote healthy flesh, until they are healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve bothers you or the main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with things that promote flesh growth until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you have not gone to the root of the problem:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if you uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pincers, pull it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and leave none;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture resists, and there is no mistake or fear, then cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them at once, put on the wound something that will cause rot, and leave it until the area around the bones is rotten, and then the bones will be easier to remove;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then only restrain the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if a large part of it is corrupted, and reaches the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it should be scraped and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cured until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, until the matter reached his leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to avoid opening it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physicians, in their folly, worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared that all emitted pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians applied treatments for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and what flowed through the holes with great force;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's body was becoming red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I inserted a tent into one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one was coming against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned away what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except what I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with healing remedies for a long time, and it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and I cleaned it, and then removed it, and I struggled to heal the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not until I cut around a palm's width of bone, and the wound was completely exposed, then I restored it with remedies;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was quickly healed and healed, and no further work was needed except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the bloodletting, he often coughed, but he was completely healed, and a hard tissue grew in place of the bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or opposition at all, neither in the present nor in the future.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place on the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a bandage, and tie it to the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another bandage of wool thicker than the first bandage, and bind it over the flesh that is over the bone, and extend the head, so that you pull the corrupted flesh downwards, and expose the flesh above the place where you want to work, so that the wire does not pierce the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a brand or a board under the bone to help cut the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and work this way as long as you can see and feel the corruption, and do this again and again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and is not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a brand underneath, and then cut along the corruption from one side to the other, and let the cut be the length of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and cut the bone where it is on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the finger of the foot, that is a very strong thing, but nevertheless you must investigate this corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the tools and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore, for each type of work, it is necessary to prepare its own tool;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the tool you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the types of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	therefore, consider the tool you need, according to what is suitable.
dou feu	from fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can dislocate either inwardly or outwardly;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corrosion with medicinal cures, and they do no good, then it is necessary to cut that limb down to where the corrosion is, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater harm, which is the loss of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and after the blackness, that corrosion spreads from limb to limb, and takes hold throughout the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	so hurry to cut it, and if it is from the sting of some venomous creatures, like sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, cut it and do not give it space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not spread to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there are no strong remedies that equal the extent of its power;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, cut it after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of cutting or severing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and have some attendants pull one of the bandages downwards, and other attendants the other bandage upwards, and you separate the flesh between the two bandages to a width of one span, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or sever it, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the severed part does not touch the healthy area, and the patient does not suffer further injury or infection.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bandage the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to a man on his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a dark discoloration that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came to his toe of the foot, until it affected his entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and a long time later, the corrosion returned to the toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling things after cleansing his body, and the corrosion could not stop;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die, for the man's strength was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land, and quickly cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have written this account only so that others might do likewise if they have need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess occurs in a fleshy area, and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and punctures, and the pus escapes, and the area remains empty, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is as thin as fine cloth, and does not reach down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain," and not "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches down to the bone deep within, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you should cut the skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not become worse due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you suspect that the skin is inflamed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with an enema thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	See if the swelling is large, and the discharge from it has a foul odor, then treat it with an enema of Egyptian medicine, which is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take vinegar, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and inject it into the swelling, and compress the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this often, until the swelling is healed and the odor is gone;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes, when this medicine is not available, enemas of ash water are given, where you take ashes from a vine branch, pour water over them, and let it settle, and use it for an enema, until you know the swelling is thoroughly cleaned;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then give him an enema of water and honey, or a little ground litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you give him an enema of honey and diluted wine, for the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine helps dry the swelling;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and are confident that the swelling is thoroughly cleaned, then give him an enema of what will cause flesh to grow there, and take a diaphanous plaster made with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you give him an enema of some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have discussed when dealing with ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the swelling is small, and the tip of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with an iron, and insert a tent of Egyptian or basil ointment until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then stitch it, leaving only the area where the enema can enter, and if the discharge opening is on top, cut it or at a lower location.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the swelling is deep, it will not allow flesh to grow there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cut the swelling from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the swelling runs to the lowest possible location; for when the swelling is deep, it will not allow flesh to grow there, and if you cannot cut the swelling from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the swelling runs easily downward, and leaves nothing of the swelling;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to put over the wound, and spread over it a linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut as strongly as necessary at the opening of the wound, a bit wider than the first one; then spread a soft ointment onto another cloth, according to the size of the opening, and put it over the opening of the wound to ease the swelling, and do not remove the large cloth entirely except once after many days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one that is over the opening of the wound, remove frequently to remove the swelling, and know whether what flows from the swelling is venom, pus, or sufficient, or digested, or indigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is spread in such a manner, and you see the nature that rises above the opening of the wound, know that the wound is healing now, and health is approaching;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the wound discharges indigested swelling after many days, know that the wound is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom flows after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men for whom the healing of flesh in their wounds takes a long time, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if indigested swelling bursts from the wound after many days, know that the wound is not healing;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the wound is slow to heal, and is prolonged, add drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointments defined, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diafinit ointment, and they make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with equal parts old wine;
puis le confit et en use;	Then apply it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And this same thing works better cooked and thickened, when diafinit ointment is unavailable, or you take myrrh and aloes and frankincense, and grind it, and powder it over the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then stick it with a bandage, and spread it over the wound, and sometimes an experienced herbalist applies long iris roots, and roots of the celestial lily, which is like the flour of vetch and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And use it in simple or compound forms:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them, and make a powder, and put it over the honey I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and is causing pressure on the bone, or the hard tissues, or the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the cure for the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panaricium is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or perhaps arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it has aged, and one does not take care of it, then a hot abscess arises and runs and casts pus until it runs to the root of the nail, and perhaps it runs the whole nail;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corrosion reaches the bone, until there is foul pain, and the fingertip is swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is not effective, you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail with a hot iron, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to prick and wound it, you must put a wedge under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it upward, and carefully and gently cut away the flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove it all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it, and remove it forcefully, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the finger decaying, cut it in half as previously described, then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is struck, and pushed, and feels great pain, you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the spatulim with a sharp blade, cutting across it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on that soothes it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the sore in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The swelling that arises in the hands of some people by chance is all fleshy, and sometimes it has bones, and sometimes a nail, and some of them arise at the root of the joint, or the origin is in some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	The one that arises on any part of the finger does not change, and the one that arises at the joint of the finger, perhaps changes.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of the fleshy one is small, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	The one that arises at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	So hold it from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which arises or ought to arise at the back, you must first cut the round flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable blade for that, then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the fingers together comes from birth, or from a wound's healing, or from a fire burn, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You should cut that swelling, so that the fingers repair according to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not fuse together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of thin lead, until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of these fingers with the palm, cut that swelling as appropriate.
des vils	of the vile.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large veins wrapped up, full of melancholy superfluities, that come in many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more happen in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give him an emetic at times, and then the root of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of iron is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are cut, and black blood is drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you tie the vein, and draw all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, apply a very hot water to the leg, so that the large blood is refined, then hold the patient's leg from the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in one, or two or three places, with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that produce black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of it is according to this method:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the patient's leg, if it has much hair, then put it in a bath, and warm the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then heat it by fire, and then cut it along the vein from the top of the knee, or in the area below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with a knife, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then put the knife underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then cut it with the knife lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the knife, as you did before, and cut it with another knife, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then lift it and cut it at the toe, then pull it and lift it down to the second incision;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it from incision to incision until it is all out, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then put a needle with a very strong double thread, and tie it and pull it, and put a knife underneath, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, put moistened wool on the wound's location in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vision is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistedly, but do not cut it at all;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vision is curved, and does not cut straight, so that it does not cut the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is intertwined in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and perhaps it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes beneath the skin, just as it comes inside the body of serpents and worms, intertwined between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes to the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head appears, you should wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half to two ounces, and the knot, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time a bit comes out, wrap it around the lead and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a portion, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will return into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot in that place and a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long or ten, and a man came to me, from whom it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, it opens one vein or hole, and pierces it to the bottom, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the matter within be emptied, and administer remedies to the place to prevent any rot for a while, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many holes appear in it, and from which many branches spring.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This ailment is called "ox disease" in our land, because it frequently occurs in oxen, and is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it clearly moving from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin wherever it goes, and causes pustules to form;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is engendered by the corruption of certain humors, as are worms and serpents and leeches and ascarids in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, for when it travels through the body and ascends to the head, and it reaches the eye, it may, by chance, enter and destroy the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you wish to treat and extract it, one can only do so when it moves.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut above it and pull it out forcefully, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire above it, until it dies;
