et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it causes is that it infects the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, then firmly press the eyebrow below it, then cut above it, and pull it out forcefully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient should use cleansing remedies and dissolving medicines for the bad putrid humors, and should avoid foods that promote putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that occurs in some limbs, and can move from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I saw it rise afterwards, like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like quick silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left that spot, and settled into the shoulder, and then a little later ran through the whole body, until it went to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it went around the body repeatedly, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had seen many others who had seen pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it like this in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had a thin body, and the veins exposed, and for that the constriction appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then treat it from above and below quickly, and then cut until the constrained wind from the place is released.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those that expel winds, like fetid pills, and pills of seraphim, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and welded;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two angles, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in chief members, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if you must then abstain from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deep, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls into it and pierces the bone, and the skin over the brain is torn, are when there is blindness and suddenness and weakness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps there is blood coming from the nostrils or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes white moisture resembling pus, and also burning flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then consider the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow hitting the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, and not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like pus, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know without doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that hits the lung is that frothy blood spurts from the wound, the throat swells, the patient's complexion changes, and they sigh loudly and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits the covering of the breast, it is near the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and great sorrow and sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the shoulder members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps some undigested food spurts from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and some straw leaps out through the intestines, there is no hope for treatment, nor for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and urine spurts out and flows away, and the patient feels intense pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, shoulder joint, spine of the back, arms, thighs, and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I removed it, and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healthy without trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I removed an arrow that had struck him in the eye's fat under the eyelid below, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach the tip towards the shaft.  The arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, and light as any iron arrow without feathers.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The man was healthy, and no bad accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I soothed the swellings, and proceeded carefully until I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I removed an arrow from a man, that had struck him in the abdomen, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and extracted it, and it was fully removed, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man whose arrow struck his back, and the wound was closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions, nor did he find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, whom an arrow struck in his face, and his wound was closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I treated an arrow in a man of the king's princes, which had struck him in the middle of his nose, and was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had been embedded for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it with a very fine probe, and felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt a prick and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I applied a drawing and digestive plaster to the area, so that the area wouldn't swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the wound from the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster again, and the wound healed completely, and the patient remained like that for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to the wound repeatedly until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow becoming loose in the wound.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I added more of that sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And the wound remained open for about four months, then it grew wider so that I could insert pliers and move it from side to side, but it would not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I continued to devise and experiment with various instruments, until I finally used strong pliers, according to the method described at the end of this chapter, so that I extracted it and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have told you the nature of extracting certain arrows, so that you may apply your treatment to what I have not said, because the book cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters, looking at even small things, and at what is present and deficient, invent new works and new instruments for the removal of strange occurrences that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are stuck except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that goes out through where it enters, this is an arrow that has entered into fleshy places, and sometimes goes out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it has rotted, and the exit is eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it doesn't, pierce around it with a very fine tool, until the surrounding area is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not remove it, but leave it until it is even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains several days without bad symptoms, then devise a way to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be removed, apply drills around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged within the body where it cannot be seen, then seek it throughout the entire area;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, remove it with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the arrow's depth, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then enlarge the wound;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and remove the arrow if you can; and if the arrow has barbs by which it is held, remove the flesh that is pierced by the barbs as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can remove it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully ensure that you do not break the arrow, so that you can remove it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then remove it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is making you uneasy, then apply what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can remove the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid there is; and if you cannot, place him according to the signs they show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or if anything is visible from it, or the skin is swollen in a place that can be seen or felt clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut above it until the pliers can grasp it, and then pull it out:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand round and round until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for a while, and then start pulling it out again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is in it, push it all the way through with the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft fell, and you want to administer a push, then administer a sharp instrument so that the arrowhead enters the tip of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push firmly, and if the arrow is sharpened, push an instrument with a pointed end into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the foot or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close, and you can cut above it, then cut there;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then remove it, and then stitch up the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many kinds of them:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, like this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tongs for pushing and for grasping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one bleeds are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen in the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two arteries that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins commonly bled from are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste," and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and is above the fossa, and is the one from which one bleeds, which is clearly visible above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and the pinky finger, and has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the curve of the shin on the left side, and the second is the saphenous one at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse," which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are near the ears helps with old colds and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the spot where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient strains their neck with a vise, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then take them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bleed from there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein in two with your two fingers, and make the blood come out as much as you want;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	Bleeding from the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic migraine, and gout, and habitual ophthalmia, and for acute tearing in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bleeding are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient should tighten their neck, so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed from the inside;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the heart above the vein towards your index finger, and place the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upward, and cut it, as you did with the two other veins, and make the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place some cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cutting and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the vein of the forehead is as effective as bloodletting from the cephalic vein in illnesses of the face, old ones, and migraines, and inflammation;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the method is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "the digger," of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press upon it with your hand, or something else, and allow blood to issue according to the quantity you desire;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary for the flame to be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and hold it sideways, for the bone is near, and perhaps the flame will break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cautery of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts aids the eyes, and the eyelid, and redness, and the ulcer in the eye, and the illnesses of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their cautery is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting with a bandage, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then cauterize, and let the cautery be across, a little bit long, a little bit wide of the flame, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind over with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The cautery of the vein of the nose is good for ague, and for sudden madness, and for facial ailments, like migraines and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the procedure for the cautery is that the patient should tighten their neck, then hold their nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long flame and place it between the lip, in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein is not clearly visible there, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The cautery of the two temples aids in constriction of the throat, and in the beginning of a fever, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in ulcers, and in herpes, and in boils;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the procedure for the cautery is that the patient should tighten their neck from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and let the patient sit upon a chair, then cauterize the vein along a small area, and draw the blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tie both veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the cautery of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cautery of the veins of the lips above helps with running sores in the mouth, and with corruption of the gums, and fissures of the lips, and of the nose and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the cautery are to make the patient sit in front of you, and tighten their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being dark, and because around them are small dark veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and likewise do with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the cautery beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cautery of the veins beneath the tongue helps after the cautery of the cephalic vein, and is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the cautery is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a dark vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then cauterize one and the other, and do not go too deep, for the arteries are underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the chest that are commonly cauterized are cauterized according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with a broad, pointed flame, or a subtle, olive-like cutting tool, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are broad or subtle according to the breadth and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame-pointed cautery tool is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And is useful for opening the hair-like veins full of visible thick blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of the olive-pointed cautery tool:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for lancing the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The lancing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps the ailments that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the lancet-wielder that he lance wisely, and that he guard against the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a hemorrhage of blood comes, then it must be stanched, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pricking, but cutting, like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein is not clearly visible, then you must constrict it, and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want some branch of it, or you lance into the vein in the middle of the arm instead:
elle apert manifestement;	it appears clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the knife flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location for the lancing, then first you should constrict the arm, so that you touch the location until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location with a point, then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a burning knife;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the area inflamed, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	Then wipe it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it emerge upward like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your finger on it for a while, then remove your finger if the blood stops, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind the arm, and leave it like that, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be careful, and not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood does not stop, and it overcomes you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for the head is pulling it away;
et estainche li sans.	and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a fig bark, and split it, and take one of the halves, and bind it firmly until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the blood stops, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it as we have said, with the powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of it is not difficult in many conditions due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein's bleeding in the middle aids in drawing blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And the practitioner must be careful of the nerve below, and if it pierces too deeply, and finds the nerve, it swells and the wound is difficult, and perhaps will not heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you should cauterize it with a cauterizing instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And cauterize the nerve as much as you are able.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed by pricking the olive-shaped vein or the myrtle-shaped vein, for it is the safest of all veins, as it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must seek the easiest spot, and do no harm if one fails the first time, and one tries again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps the spot swells in some people when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only administered to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are in the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, basilic, and median cubital;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered to illnesses has no set time, but that when needed, by day or by night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying a child except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And the elderly who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a mild clyster, if they have retained much waste, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the putrid superfluities harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor should those who are overly full of food, or who are drunk, as long as they are intoxicated, or those who are hydrops, be bled;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should be wary of bleeding after a colic attack, and vomiting, and loose bowels, and multiple pregnancies in women, and labor, and prolonged wakefulness and fasting, and anything that drains all the strength, either of the spirit or the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then thin out the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm near the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from work, and from hardship, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be cheerful and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the person being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tie the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands, until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then the bleeder moistens the flame with a little old oil, then puts his left hand's finger on the vein under the area where he wants to bleed, so that the vein doesn't burst and fail when he strikes.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like ropes when bled, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when the flame is put on, it recoils, and the vein cannot open, and so it is with those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bleeder must be careful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then try again a little below that spot or above it quickly, if the spot is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the spot is swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps a hot abscess will come.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter a bath, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you fear it will not release as much blood as you want, then apply fire directly to the opening itself;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and treat it a little hastily, before the spot is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, then do not restart the bleeding, and apply a little linseed oil, for it thins the blood, and linseed is gentler in this place than oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil to each bleeding you make to the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing does heal and soothe them, when put on the area;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so it thins the blood and disperses it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which happens many times, especially when the bleeding is not sufficient to the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and place on the area a sponge moistened in warm water and salt, and keep it on for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood leaves the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains in the area after a few days, it does no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, put on some aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and appearance happen with the bleeding of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, do not put anything on it that we have mentioned, for perhaps it is flowing from the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it issue until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it be until it is thinned;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the incision be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let him be bled little and often, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of bloodletting is safe from the flow of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is better than letting blood from long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body weakens during bloodletting, give bread soaked in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is hot, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold disposition, before the bloodletting, let him eat bread soaked in syrup of roses, or in syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bloodletting, after the flow of much blood, he should drink broth of meat, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to let air out of his arm, and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by extensive bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to let air out of their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, let them bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another part, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening so that it drips in abundance;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	after you have observed all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on their pulse while they bleed, so that death does not come in place of abundance, and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate when you wish to release the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	or if it is bent, that he extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it bleeds a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you prick it with the tip of the flame, so that the blood that has clotted in the opening of the vein flows out forcefully, and put a small piece of salt mixed with water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it at all until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is lanced in place of the vein of the head because it is compound.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the veins are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is tied moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, then bleed through the middle, not from the side nor lengthwise;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let it bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot issue forth, then put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back into hot water, for one puts it more into water in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Bleeding from the vein of the right hand is good for all liver ailments, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the blood flows sideways, and if you cut it completely across, nothing will harm;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as you need, then put oil and a bandage on the vein to quickly close it, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting in the left hand is good for the disease of mice, and do everything as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bloodletting from the saphena vein is good for all diseases below the body, such as diseases of the groin, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the method of this bloodletting is that the patient puts their foot in hot water, and rubs the vein until it bursts, and binds the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many veins go.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So bleed it then at the larger vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed it above the foot, watch out for the nerves below, and bleed through as if cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, return the foot to the water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the lancing fails the first time, start again a little higher the second time, for the place is sore.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	and do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise on the other foot's sole.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its lancing is worthwhile for hip pain, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its lancing is that the patient enters a bath, and tightens above the ankle with four fingers twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, lance it in every way you can, and in a crosswise manner;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the location is safe, and it is very responsive to hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, lance any vein that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let as much blood flow as you wish, and then loosen the bandage, and place cotton on it and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that is without striking is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either by total fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is right on top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and another is in the middle of the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping between the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the cupping does not draw much blood, except for small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore does not weaken one, as does bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not appropriate to administer it, either with fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to the necessity of illnesses or custom, cupping is needed, administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and cough up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we instruct them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The leeches from the temple assist the pressure on the head...that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the entire body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of the leeching of the cephalic vein, and it is not appropriate for those of cold complexion to use it, or those who have a cold, for it does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it is not appropriate for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold illnesses in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed from it become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilica vein, and therefore it is good for tightness in the breast, and for a fissure in the windpipe, and for coughs, and for congestion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be applied gently, for if it holds too firmly, it induces forgetfulness in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bleeding from the basilica vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you should instruct the master to press his hand firmly upon applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there is no excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for gum decay, and similar illnesses in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is a substitute for bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for diseases caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as bleeding from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from those large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the master not to press too deep, for the area is bare of flesh, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	Cupping on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below, and the cup should be large, and made of brass, because it needs to draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps, if it were small, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	And it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping on the legs bleeds openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the kidneys, and bladder, and remove the impurities.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And are in the place of the two shins, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause swelling in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the cupping is to first place it empty, and suck gently, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from this, until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, lift it, and replace the cupping glasses, and watch the condition of the body, for there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	So it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and somewhat deep.
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw little by little blood, we need only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we begin again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the outcome is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with arousing and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	whether it is of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or of lily oil, or of chamomile oil, or other similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take amarantin oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and the similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is cupped has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil there, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or blackberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or other similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them be lifted with willow or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities are lifted with old wine, or with sea water, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not be cupped with a cupping glass before a bath or in a bath, but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he wash himself when he is to be cupped and when he is cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And be careful if the one who is being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in moderation, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat poults, and hare's meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and medium-aged fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat poults and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day that he will take a purgative, he ought to drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or nutmeg before the purgative, or afterwards, to strengthen the principal limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be diluted, but it is by no means fitting that those who are hot drink it.
