Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping that is applied without striking is that which is applied to the liver, and the spleen, and gout, and to the belly and the flank and the kidneys and the hip, for those limbs do not endure being struck on them, and one does not apply it there except to draw blood from limb to limb, just as we apply it to the breasts when the nipple bleeds;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, just as we apply cupping to the belly and the flank to thin the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain, when there is obstruction or a stone, and it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus does it when it is applied to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cuppings are administered empty just to suck;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in illnesses of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping with warm water alone, or with water in which one has boiled suitable herbs for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And have two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side near the middle one small hole, as for putting in a needle, and be of bronze, soft in front so that it does not harm the patient when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in the middle a crosswise rod of bronze or iron, for putting in a lit candle, and there be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cuppings of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cupping on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or a lining, and place it in the middle of the cupping through the rod that is in the middle of the cupping, so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your fingers be on the opening that we have spoken of, so that when one wishes, the vapor will go forth, and one removes the cupping;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one takes the lining again as before, and one repeats it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping, then, that is applied in a pleurisy, acute, there is no rod or opening, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed upon the limb simply;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are only applied to limbs where one cannot put cupping because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places bare of flesh, such as the toe or nose, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clear, soft, unblemished water, without any injury, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water for a time, until they are well-filled, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then the patient should be bled from a vein and cupped, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, then apply it, for this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then cleanse the area with warm water, and then dry it well;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area heals too quickly after the leeches, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and apply it, until the blood is drawn out;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is increased, then apply crushed vitriol, or gallstones, or similar things, until it is drawn out;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place half peeled beans on the area and leave them until they burn the area, it will now draw it out;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take more leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches do not want to take hold, then rub the area with fresh blood, or you pierce it with a needle until blood comes out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will adhere;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you want them to fall off, then sprinkle some powdered alum and salt, or ash, on them, they will fall off now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that fools scorn this chapter, as if they never saw any of the ancient books, nor read a single letter in them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge is rare in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and through experiment, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained within, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we state in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and remain upon the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break, dislocation, twist, or fracture occurs to anyone, you should quickly bleed the patient on either side, if nothing else prevents you, such as weakness of the body, or childhood, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold meats, that is to say, cold joints, and the flesh of birds and young bucks, and drink no wine, and eat no fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, so that you are not in doubt of a hot abscess, nor of the spreading of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to his former way of life.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, the patient should be nourished with foods that promote growth, or that have viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and marrow, and feet, and cow's belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the fracture heals more quickly and easily.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal or mend properly according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is a treatment, to set the broken bone in strong bandages that hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not to cut the work entirely, and therefore he must be nourished with hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the chest, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes in one direction, and another in a different direction, as when the tip of a feather for writing is sharpened.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each kind has its own method, and its own specific instrument in restoration, according to what comes to remember its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that its place is twisted, and it shows clearly by pressing, and it sounds when the hand is pressed;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may well have twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If so, you should not move it by hand, but apply medicines that come later, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that a fracture that extends to the joint, and the two parts are separated, they must now be put in perfect alignment, lest a hot abscess come there;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if a hot abscess comes there, leave it for a few days, until the abscess is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it in alignment as gently and wisely as you can, and know that the restoration of one is easier than that of one where there are pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it, as it should be later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is split in two parts, whether it's the hand or the foot, or in your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you return all the additions to their places as gently as you can, and take care that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well join the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you straighten it beautifully, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those who, through their work, cause heat and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, then restrain the patient well so that he does not move it, neither when awake nor when asleep, nor when turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and carefully watch that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it must be put in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that it is put straight, that no twisting comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the fractured limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that fractured limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap with soft and subtle linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and bind it evenly on all sides, so that there is no mark;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind around light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture is then slightly separated;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large portion of the healthy place, then take another bandage, and turn it around again over the fractured place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go again to the part below the fracture, and tighten it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first bandage above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put linen padding or cloths between the bandages, until it is all even, then bind everything over the bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put on something soothing to the abscess that is hot, and that removes the swelling, and leave it like that for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then tighten over your splints, and they should be half the width of a cleverly cut cane, or of wood from which cleaves are made, or of palm ribs, and should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint placed over the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as is suitable for the limb's size or stature;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten over the splints just as you did for the first bandaging, then tie a suitable thread over it, as in the first bandaging over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter on top, gradually less so;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the thread should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, like the works of fools who make their bandages from twisted linen cords, and that is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not fitting that there be less than a finger's width of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after tightening in healthy places, then place linen or wool padding under them, so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to bind all fractured limbs with splints on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply splints forcefully until after 5 days or 7, or more, depending on your certainty of a hot abscess occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that adheres to the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of plaster for restoring fractures in many cases, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take 3 drachms of abareis and ladani and enule and asafetida and gum arabic and mugat, each 10 drachms.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloes, each 5 drachms;
alechil VIIII З.;	Alechil 9 drachms;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the man's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another type of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and comfrey, each 10 drachms;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, each 9 drachms;
acaice VI З.;	gum arabic 6 drachms;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armenian bole 10 drachms, and grind well, and mix with water or the white of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and for bones separated from their places, and it soothes the pain arising, and for the use of the bone, and the fracture:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and leaves of wild poppy, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the healing of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and vetch flour, one part of each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them, and mix with wine; and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger plaster than the first, for when a hard abscess comes after the limb is restored.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of mallow, flaxseed, baluster, melilot, and plantain, and violet and chamomile flowers, one part of each.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind them, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore strength anything other than a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on the broken limb, for restoration, slightly warm dry things, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another type of plaster that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and cut human hair, or bird feathers, and vismalve, and oak bark, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove it a little later, and watch to see if the patient feels no pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not, do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, lack of rest, or swelling, then hurry, and remove it, and take the plaster away now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, and apply to the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then leave the limb to rest for an hour, then place dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bandage for a night, until you are sure of a hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is gone, then resume the gentle bandaging, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling are entirely gone, and you need plaster and a bandage, then begin again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not unbind it until after three or four or five or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals and the flesh grows together.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then restrain it more than before, and increase its nourishment, as I said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm water frequently whenever you unbind it, every third day, and loosen the bandage a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	By this work then comes nourishment to the limb, and amends quickly what foolish doctors do, who restore the limb crookedly.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is bad, and such work is fearful, and I see no other remedy than to leave it alone and work it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many types of fractures exist, and diverse forms, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by blows from a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone down to the surface beneath the bone, like a branch or a log does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason this type of fracture is called "haunchure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword cuts the bone from above, piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound from these two fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow-in, or a fissure, or a blow from a stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fissure is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and it causes a piece of bone to move inwards, and the place is fractured as when blacksmiths strike on kettles;
si entre li piere dedens.	if a stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those whose bones are moist or soft, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are detached, like splinters;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the detachment on them, and the examination by probes, and by the corrupted flesh on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when the bone is uncovered, and you rub on top, the broken black bone appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be mindful of the patient's complications, and if you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, numbness, acute fever, eyes swelling and turning red, and other similar conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see terrifying complications, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is in winter, then the bone should be removed before the fourteenth day, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue beneath the bone is corrupted, and the complications that we have mentioned appear.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue covering the brain, then you must split the fractured part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you should take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in every way you can, and over the wound's surface as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or a pus-filled abscess, then aid as necessary, and you should fill the area with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and rest the wound until the pus-filled abscess is calmed, and be assured of any bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two types of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is that you cut at a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then add another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of tempered iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must pierce around it, rather than making incisions with awls, not deeply enough to pierce the bone of the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the point, so that the point does not pass through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you need several, so that each one fits into its place on the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for all skulls;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place an awl on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then reposition the awl elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with the knives the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you pull the bone out with your hand, or with any of the instruments you have, such as pliers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, you must then cut the rough edges that remain on the bone using any other instrument similar to a knife, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other knife;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is that which Galen described, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the ligament very strongly, and that is his saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone, where the fracture is apparent, so that, once you have uncovered that part, you place the head of this lancet-shaped incisor beneath the head of the fracture, whose shape is this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut it on one side only, and it has a sharp edge on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike lightly with a small mallet, so that you cut the bone slightly all around, and take good care of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhering to the bone, then remove it gently, for one removes it well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the cloth, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, then you must remove that rough spot, and remove the scales with a fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to administer the most suitable one in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use larger rasps first, and then finer ones, and do not cease from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other cuts and subtle fractures, you must administer treatment according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something not to be overlooked by one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as possible, so you do not burden the surface, then administer another bandage on top, and do not bind it too tightly, only just enough to hold the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one or two days, until the inflamed abscess is soothed, then unbind it, and apply medicines like lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and place it over the wound, and apply remedies, healing without causing pain;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and watch that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave ointment there, nor allow pus to collect, for when pus collects on the membrane of the brain, it will rot and fester, and great harm will come to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one places a biting substance on the surface, it will burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, beware, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening appears there, only because of the medicine placed on it, that such a virtue has, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix them together, and put it on the surface;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with the appropriate methods of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your index finger in the nostril, and place the broken part of the nose against your index finger, and hold it in place, until the nose returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you should place it even with the top of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do the same again, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess is calmed, then apply strips of linen to the bridge of the nose, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you put one on the other side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the strips be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say one should soak the strips in butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they must be soaked in a mixture of egg white and flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the strip until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes goose feathers are put in the nose in place of strips, and a soft bandage is wrapped around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through it;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil comes to the nose while you are working on it, put a plaster or soaked cotton in rose oil, or a bit of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if a boil doesn't come, put a plaster on the outside, of millet flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light wicks on top, and do not tie the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nose fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then stitch the fissure, and treat it with things that bind flesh, and make it stick together, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and put lead strips on it, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only on the outside, and is not broken in two, except for the inside bumps, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, put your right index finger in, and gently push the fracture inwards, and with the other hand, align it from the outside, and make it level.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two, you must administer extension on both sides, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth move or break, bind them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place a plaster on the fractured jaw, and put a double cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place a large, well-made splint, or a piece of leather, equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it over it as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, unbind it on the third day, and then readjust what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster of flour from the mill, with plenty of egg or linseed flour, after you have removed the plaster;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster dries, and the patient's condition doesn't change, leave it until healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, check to see if any piece of bone has been removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If subtly removed with suitable instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remains, close the wound, if it is large, and put suitable dressings on it to generate flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forceps break many times before, toward the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is breakage with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the breakage is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken forceps;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck toward the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture evenly with your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as you need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the forceps, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you place the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out, because it goes deep, then the patient must lie often on his/her back, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and the attendants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then align the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, you must split it open.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and carefully pull the pieces apart, and if the bone cannot join by any means, cut it with one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you place this instrument under the forceps, to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two edges, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound you made when you pulled the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, soak the bandages in rose oil, and oil, and wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The treatment of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you place on the bone a plaster of mill powder and egg white, and place light cloths on top, and place a splint under the arm, if you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then put a double bandage over the cloths and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the splint over the break, and turn the bandage over the shoulder, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and keep it in place on each side, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the splint does not move from the broken bone, keep checking it daily, and when the splint loosens, tighten it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and lay the patient on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	so that the fracture will be relieved from the strain by raising the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the shoulder, and do not loosen it until twenty days, unless bad accidents occur;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then renew the plaster, if you see that it needs it, and tighten and leave it thus, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in the most cases within twenty-eight days, and in fewer for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes the shoulder breaks in a broad area or in the middle, and one only knows it is broken by feeling it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you align it according to the shape of the fracture, and reposition it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the area flour from the mill, with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and place over it a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put over it a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the splint there is a gap anywhere on the shoulder, fill that gap with linen bandages, so that the splint lies flat;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and examine the bandage every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it softens, bind it more tightly, and make the splint level if it has moved from its place, and let the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is complete, unbind it, and be sure, for it is not bone that easily moves out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and is a little below the skin, cut it open, and remove it, and do as we have said in the chapter on treating abscesses by heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the breast.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The breast is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the edge.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of breath, and sickness, and perhaps vomits blood, and the ends of the broken bone show, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and they put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and join the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and subtly adjust it to all the ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place plasters and bandages over the delicate bone fragments, or another light material, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the broken bone so it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and tighten it properly, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be loosened, due to corrosion or itching that arises in the area, or pain or abscess, hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and address whatever has occurred through appropriate treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then replace the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs usually occurs only in the thick parts behind the back, and at the top inside, and they only break because they are brittle;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well upon questioning the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the break straight, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the broken ribs are tilted inward, the patient feels great pain and pricking, as if from stabbing, because the bone is piercing the tissue;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and breathes in gasps, and coughs and vomits great amounts of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancients have given much thought to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest a hot abscess appear, if it has not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has appeared, let it be treated.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some of you say that one places cupping glasses on the spot, to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the cupping glasses will not draw superfluities to the spot due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that one should cover the spot with wool soaked in warm oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly apply the bandage around it, then be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, diet, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels intense pain that he cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and doubt exists in the patient, it is necessary to cut into the spot where the rib is broken, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the surface.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one should cut the bone, and pull gently, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if hot abscesses come, then place cloths moistened in rose oil on the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as appropriate for an abscess, and let him lie often on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the neck, and little happens to bend it.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, watch if you see their hands softened and swollen and lifeless, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they don't feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many ways, and if they move and feel well when squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the sick person will be cured, if treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, watch if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in the hands, and on the back, have wind and expulsion without will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is laid on its stomach, there is expulsion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is laid on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Then do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not come to him, the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that if there is a hot abscess, you put rosemary oil or egg oil on it until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is separated, it is necessary to cut around the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, and then treat it with an ointment that generates flesh, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone of the arm, which is called the "arm bone", is broken, place your left hand's pouch on it, and try to set it straight with your other hand, then apply a plaster and splint, if you need them;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then bind it, and if there are any separated bones, cut around them, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes the hip bone is broken, and if it is, there is not much of a lessening at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it cuts lengthwise, and tilts inward, and the patient experiences pain and throbbing, and the broken part swells.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand above, so that you are above the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what the fracture is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then place the fracture evenly, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it tilts inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it in line, then place the plaster over it, then place a wooden or leather splint over it, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and fill the space below the ribs, so that the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess comes there, do not touch it until the hot abscess is calmed, and place upon it what we have previously said;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and bind it as necessary, if there is no bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, it should be restored according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie to the two ends two straps, and hang them upwards, and let the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then place the broken arm over the wood, until it reaches the armpit, and have a curve of wood in the middle, then hang it over something heavy or the attendant stretches it downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then let the attendant align the fracture with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that you support the patient on a stretcher, and tie the hand to their neck, then instruct two attendants that one holds that which is above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds below with a strap, and each stretches to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the extraction to be stronger, tighten one strap below the fracture, and one above the fracture, and each of the attendants stretches to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is close to the shoulder joint, you must place one strap below the armpit, and another towards the elbow, below the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, you must place a strap lightly, without effort, until the fracture is aligned in its place, and towards the elbow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then align the fracture as it should be, and secure it, if no suppurative swelling comes.
