Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocation, hurry to turn the joint, and extend it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	Perhaps it will return, and no other cure is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare a strong assistant, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another assistant extends their hand above in such a way that they put their hands under their armpits, then tightens it with a soft strap over the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the strap;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and all pull upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then treatment must be applied to its similar case.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is inside, you should place the patient on their healthy side, then place the strap on the root of the thigh, and the place under the armpit, then extend the strap upwards towards the armpit, and towards the collarbone;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then take other assistants by their arms, and embrace the large part of the injured thigh, and extend it outwards forcefully:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	then it will return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this type of dislocation is less severe than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot straighten it in this way that we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft strap around the two heels and the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two inches more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then be hung over the top of a post, and be two arms' length above the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct one assistant to grasp the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who grasps firmly the thigh, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in the outer part, the patient should lie down, as we have said for those with gibbosity, and tighten a bandage around the injured leg properly and also around the foot;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two embers, one at the head and one at the feet, then place one ember between the patient's thighs in the middle of the shape;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have wet cloths placed around it so it does not injure the patient, then let each assistant pull towards himself, and the most skilled one should put the dislocation even with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it as we have said for gibbosity, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and let the skilled one put his effort on the affected arm, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the patient downwards, nor to lift him from the ground, but it is necessary that he be as if the hip were dislocated behind, as we have said concerning lying on both hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let him lie on his face, and the bandage be extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be fixed when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then join the thighs, and apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and apply the plaster again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are equal, then bind it, as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then unbind it, and let it move gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward and outward, and backward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you order the patient to bend their leg to their thigh, and if it does not fit into their thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their face, and place their foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another attendant should extend their foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that their leg fits well against their thigh easily;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and place the plaster on it, and make the leg fit against the thigh, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then unbind them;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient should not exert themselves to walk, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not fully recovered, the attendant should apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes dislocated completely, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and protruding towards the side where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is gentle, and it should be gently stretched with the hands when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and two assistants hold the leg firmly above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the foot towards your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and place the foot firmly upward.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that is good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If not, then start the work again, for it returns.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return thus, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a pole in the ground between their thighs, and tie straps around it, so that it does not injure the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then let the attendants hold the thigh, and other attendants stretch the foot to their hands or a rope, that they tie above the ankle of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then let each attendant stretch equally, and the pole should be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when stretching.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then let the physician hold the dislocation with their hands, and another attendant hold the healthy leg underneath, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, put the plaster and bandages on, and bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves above the ankle behind, that the bandages are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it two or three days, and if the bandages soften, tighten them.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he walks before that time, there is no guarantee that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil develops there, you must relieve it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they must be gently straightened without force, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface or, i.e., a table, completely straight, and place your foot on the exposed joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is aligned, and nothing is visible, you must place a board under the sole of the foot, between two supports, then hold it firmly, and leave it for three days, then release it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and allow it to rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	So do not be presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and cautious, not rash;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use soothing things at the beginning of a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reposition the limb to its place before the hot abscess reaches it;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to the hot abscess and treat the wound, as appropriate, with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones separated, then set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And beware of entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will be measured according to your Creator, and for the well-being of your soul and body.
